<Author>Enigmablue
<Content>Out the way but worth the stay The Whampoa Harbour Plaza is a little out the way as its not in the central Kowloon area but the Star Ferry across to the island is only 500m away so it still easy to get to. Its actually quite relaxing after a hard days sightseeing to have that 15 min boat ride to escape the main island. The hotel also offers a shuttle bus to the bottom of Nathan Rd. The bus also stops at Hung Hom railway station (although the bus driver was a little weird about picking people up from that stop).We had harbour view room (9th floor) and its was fairly luxurious with a great deep bath which was awesome for soothing weary bones! This was our first stop on our RTW trip and it set a high standard for the others to follow. The buffet breakfast was good but a little pricey as the Pacific Coffee Club just up the street does a decent croissant and coffee (plus free internet) for a third of the price.As for sightseeing we had an actioned packed first day where we managed to do Victoria's Peak and a little of the main island early in the morning and caught the ferry to Lantau Island to visit the big Buddha (Po Lin Monastery) in the late afternoon. HIghly recommended but only if your fit and healthy otherwise split this over two days.As for dining, we splurged a little on Aqua at 1 Peking Rd for dinner which has some awesome views but it's a little pricey. The local shops and bakeries are just as good though!

<Content>We loved this hotel We booked this hotel after reading really positive comments by other Tripadvisor members. We were not dissapointed in any way. What a lovely hotel. Sorry vedgies, but the Lobster and scallops were just fab.In short, we loved Hong Kong  Kowloon, we loved the hotel and the people are just lovely. You have to go!

<Author>FJSA
<Content>Great value hotel Due to recent troubles at Bangkok airport, had a last minute change of plans and re-routed my trip via a 4 day stop in Hong Kong- which meant I had to find a Hong Kong hotel with just one week's notice. Naturally, I turned to tripadvisor for recommendations, and found the (highly recommended) Harbour Plaza was both within my price range- and had rooms available. Don't be put off because the hotel isn't central; both the excellent shuttle service, and star ferry on the doorstep, mean that transportation is quick, clean and regular. The hotel is within easy walking distance of a range of local shops and restaurants as well. Rooms are spacious and clean, the breakfast buffet is excellent. I was offered a free upgrade to a 'superior' harbour view room, although i never worked out what was superior about it--- and the harbour views, although lovely, look across at happy valley apartment blocks, not at hong kong central skyline. In all, I wouldn't rate this hotel as 5 star, more like a good 4 star. But excellent value in a city where crazy-money is charged for accommodation. I don't hesitate in recommending it.

<Author>BigHKFan
<Content>5 Star Hotel - Excellent We stayed for 2 weeks in September on a sightseeing holiday.The hotel looks fantastic from the outside and inside is even better.The marble flooring, water fountains, majestic stone staircase, huge windows all create a sense of space and calm.Our room had a harbour view. We didn't face directly over to Central, more North Point, but even then the view out into the harbour and beyond was simply stunning. We had a 12th floor room, so were sufficiently high enough to enjoy the vista.Only gripe was the TV was a bit old fashioned but to be honest that is just nit-picking. The room was excellent.I recommend making use of the hotel leisure facilities. The glass sided rooftop pool is a great feature and one that we made lots of use of. The hotel also has a comprehensive gym. It is nice to be able to use treadmills whilst watching the boats on the harbour below.As we were on a budget as far as food was concerned, we didn't often eat in the hotel restaurants (there are 5 I believe) but when we did the food was of a high standard. We made more use of restaurants and places to eat outside the hotel, there's plenty of choice.Some have complained about the hotel's location, and whilst it is not as ideally located as, for example, the Peninsula or even YMCA, there are benefits to being located in the slightly out of the way Hung Hom. It is about 30 minutes bus journey from the airport.The area around the hotel is a more residential area with plenty of shops and small malls to cater for everyone's needs. It is also quieter and more sedate than in central TST or on the Island.Perfect to unwind in after a long day's sightseeing.Even though I would imagine Nathan Road and the Star ferry are a good 30 minute walk, the hotel does provide a free shuttle bus. We used the shuttle bus every day and it was the best way of getting around. It runs every 30 minutes into Mody Road and Nathan Road which are the places to go for food, shopping and to experience the more energetic side of Hong Kong.From there the Star Ferry is 1 minute walk, Chungking Mansions 1 minute away, Temple St Night market 4 minutes etc. If you are going to stay at this hotel, then I highly recommend using the shuttle buses.Even though the hotel is not centrally located this never proved to be a problem when it came to sightseeing and exploring. We always used the bus to get into TST then from there we took the Star Ferry over to HK Island. From there you can take another bus to Stanley and Aberdeen, ride the trams into Wan Chai, take the Peak Tram upto Victoria Peak or you can take another ferry from Central over to Lama Island.Or you can stay in TST and get the brilliant MTR over to Lantau to see the Big Buddha, Po Lin Monastery and ride the cable car.Hung Hom KCR railway is not far from the hotel should you wish to venture into the New Territories and beyond.We did all this and providing we were back at Nathan Road for the last bus, we could easily get back to the hotel.On one occasion we decided to stay out later but even getting a taxi takes no more than a few minutes from Nathan Road and costs a handful of dollars. The hotel provides a card with their address printed in Cantonese, so you can show this to the driver.Hotel staff were always very friendly and really did help us with any queries over the bill, or booking day trips such as dolphin watching etc. When my iPod couldn't be found on our leaving day, hotel staff bent over backwards to find it, which they did.All in all my 2 weeks in Hong Kong was one of the best experiences I have ever had, and the Harbour Plaza hotel made it even better.Very highly recommended.

<Author>topcop999
<Content>Woderful end to our honeymoon As a special treat for our Honeymoon we booked this hotel on our return journey to the UK from Australia. We stayed 3 nights and chose one of the harbour club rooms. These rooms are all situated on the 19th floor and the majority have a wonderful view of Victoria harbour as ours did. We specified at the time of booking we wanted a Harbour view. Being in the Harbour club gives you exclusive complimentary extras such as Continental Breakfast, Afternoon Tea and Cakes, Evening Bites and alcoholic drinks 6pm until 8pm, Fitness Centre Use, Free Laundry (Limited to one suit per day), 10% off restaurants, Late 3pm checkout, Business facilities such as use of conference room, Interpreter services, free internet access in lounge (paid access in rooms) I booked directly with the hotel seven months prior to staying and it was simple, just using their website and submitting credit card details to secure the room. Upon arrival at the hotel we attended the main desk and due to booking with the Harbour Club, were immediately ushered up to the 19th floor. Here we were able to check in at the exclusive Harbour Club reception and our luggage followed very soon after. Very efficient and just in time for complimentary evening snacks and drinks! We found all staff friendly, informative and helpful throughout our stay, in particular the staff on the Harbour Club reception. (Wendy  Tracy) The continental breakfast was not as we know it. There was everything from smoked salmon, spring rolls, sausages, eggs, fruit, cakes, etc. The rooms have excellent local information booklets, maps and a business card with the Hotel details written in Mandarin, this is ideal when getting a taxi back to the Hotel. When you leave the hotel there is always an abundance of taxis around the foyer. One of the door staff will quite happily volunteer to inform the taxi driver of your chosen destination. Taxi鈥檚 are really cheap 28HK$ (拢2.20) to Kowloon Centre (TSIM SHA TSUI). This is more ideal for after 8pm when the hotel free shuttle bus and the local Star Ferry terminal has closed. (The other Star Ferry terminals run much later) The Star Ferry terminal is literally 2 minutes walk from the hotel and goes to central HONG KONG Island and WAN CAI district on HONG KONG island every 15 minutes for fifty pence! From these ferry piers on HONG KONG Island you can easily find the MTR stations. You can then travel virtually anywhere you like on the island(s). (Including Airport, Disney World, Zoo, etc.)Anyone who describes this hotel as 鈥榦ut of the way鈥?can鈥檛 have experienced the easy transport links or is not prepared to walk more than a few hundred metres. This city is easier and cheaper to navigate than London. Even along the main Whampoa Gardens street leading up to the hotel there is a vast array of high class eateries and a few shops open until at least midnight. For me, this hotel provided a slightly less hectic base with wonderful scenic views of Victoria Harbour, especially from the roof top pool.When we arrived at the airport and went into the arrivals area we found it amass with taxi drivers touting for business. Most of them seem genuine and are quoting between 300 (拢24) and 380 Hong Kong Dollars to Kowloon. 300 Dollars is about right for the time of writing for a basic taxi. You will pay more for a limo or bigger taxi and more to Hong Kong Island itself. The genuine taxi drivers are normally well dressed with shirts and ties. Beware you will get unscrupulous ones touting for business who are only private hire or not registered taxi drivers whatsoever. If in doubt, walk out of the airport arrivals behind the MTR rail station ticket desk and choose a bonafide liveried taxi on your own judgement. MTR is the excellent underground service serving main Hong Kong Island, Kowloon and Lantau Island including the airport. It is clean, efficient, air conditioned, cheap, fast and gets to almost anywhere on the main parts of the island and peninsula.A good tip before exiting the airport is buy yourself an Octopus card from the aforementioned MTR ticket desk. This card is useable on all transport except taxi so it includes Trams, Trains, Buses, Star Ferry, etc. and also many shops such as 7/11 shop. The card costs around 50 HK$ (拢4) admin fee which is redeemable upon surrender. You then have to charge it with a minimum of 100 HK$ (拢8) and it is re chargeable at many places such as MTR stations and 7/11 shops. I only put 100 HK$ on the card and it lasted the full 3 days; I was on and off ferries, trams, buses and the MTR all day long. The MTR also runs until 1.30am!We went to Victoria Peak on Central Hong Kong Island which is accessible on foot, bus or a Tram ride up the Peak for a breathtaking view of the whole Victoria Harbour. (A clear day is a must and a night time visit worthwhile) The botanical gardens with huge outdoor aviary is worth a visit on the way there or back as it is in close proximity to the tram station.Lantau Island (Airport island) is where the Po Lin Monastery is situated. We visited this to see the BIG BUDDHA (A huge bronze Buddha) and see a fully functioning monastery where you can dine on an inexpensive sumptuous Chinese vegetarian lunch. Lantau Island is accessible via the MTR Tung Chung line and at the terminus you can take a 3.5 mile cable car right up to the monastery village or get a bus. Again the NGONG PING 360 Cable car is inexpensive (拢10) There is an abundance of restaurants and souvenir shops here.Temple Street Night Market off Nathan Road is worth a look in the Kowloon area. We got a taxi there from the hotel and later walked back along Nathan Road. The market sells all sorts from absolute junk to decent copies of everything you could imagine. (Some seems original) It鈥檚 not hard sell but vendors do pounce when you start looking at the stalls. Make sure you do your homework before you part with your precious Dollars. Some items are cheaper further along and often items are not even priced up. It is worth bartering and often you can get things for much less than half price. There is more neon here than LAS VEGAS.On our final day we took the bus from central HONG KONG Island through the island tunnel to a southern town called Stanley. Near to here is where a British Army base was situated (Fort Stanley) and it was once a quaint fishing village. It now has a Mediterranean style beachfront with a good range of eateries and a lovely stretch of beach. The market place here is probably the best market I saw in Hong Kong. No hard sell, nicely displayed goods and very friendly Vendors. Bartering is not as necessary as most things are priced up making comparison easier. There are good quality Silks, Cashmere scarfs, bags, etc. Deals are still available especially if you are purchasing multiple items.The 鈥楽ymphony Of Lights鈥?is a nightly ritual where at 8pm 23 of the hotels and business district skyscrapers display a wonderful light and laser show choreographed to music played around the Victoria Central Harbour area. There is a purpose built viewing tower on the Kowloon Side behind the main taxi and bus stand at TSIM SHA TSUI.In summary a wonderfully vibrant and clean city in the main, with so much to do we had nowhere near long enough. Watch out for some of the back street type food stalls/shops, not as clean as similar areas in the likes of Singapore. You鈥檒l be able to spot the bad ones and note that there are some unusual things on the menu. The Chinese seem to eat every part of the animal, but at the end of the day it鈥檚 all meat, albeit maybe a little gristly! If the seafood is still alive before you order it, then you should be ok! A city I will definitely re-visit and most certainly the Harbour Plaza Hotel. Some good pre reads are DK Eyewitness Guide to Hong and the AA Guide to Hong Kong. With it being such a busy and hectic 鈥榗ity鈥?it is worth hitting the ground running and knowing what you want to see. Fellow travellers enjoy!!!

<Content>harbour views? not always My husband booked the Harbour Plaza for a surprise trip. I lived in Hong Kong prior to handback and Hung Hom would not have been my first choice of location but.. was happy to take a look.On the website the hotel is impressive and as a yachtie and lover of all boats/ships he booked the harbourview room. Some people may see that the MTR has a station at hung hom but the distance to the harbour plaza is too far to walk, let alone that it's a confusing maze of roads and overpasses to negotiate if one did attempt to. The ferry is spasmodic and finishes early so taxi is the only option and the traffic formidable. I would not stay at this hotel again, I would book one on the island or Kowloon in preference.

<Author>Mariner27
<Content>Fantastic What can I say about this hotel, it is probably one of the best I have every stayed in. We were a bit dubios at first due to its location. Everyone that I had spoken to that had been to Hong Kong said that staying on Hong Kong Island however we found the location to be great. Ok it isn't amongst any of the hustle and bustle but we liked that and it was so easy to get around by taxi and the nearby star ferry terminal that we didn't feel compromised in any way. It is definately worth paying the extra for a sea view. The views are amazing and you could just sit and watch for hours, even if you look down from your room to see the joggers and tai chi -ers throughout the day. Our room was lovely, the beds were really comfortable and the linen was clean and changed regularly. The bathroom was clean and modern with both a bath and walk in shower. I also loved that there were speakers in the bathroom so you could listen to the TV or radio. The hotel also provides bathrobes and slippers which came in very handy for visiting the rooftop pool which we regularly visited. The pool area is lovely but beware, it can get a bit windy up there and the pool is freezing!Didn't really eat at the restaurants however the breakfast was superb - its definately not cheap but you can fill up on all kinds of weird and wonderful things to suit all tastes. for those who don't want to pay so much there is a coffee bean type cafe that does lovely coffees/juices and pastries for a fraction of the price. The hotel itself has a small coffee shop which do lovely cakes and coffee.The hotel staff were extremely friendly and are happy to help and recommend places. They also go out of their way to remember you name which probably is a ploy to get a tip and the end of your stay but it does make you feel welcome.Hong Kong itself is a fantastic place, its clean friendly, easy to get around with pretty much something for everyone. My personaly recommendations would be afternoon tea at the penninsula, a trip up Victoria Peak and a trip to a race meet if there is one. Stanley is also lovely if you want to venture out of the city for the day. The harbour plaza is an ideal hotel for a memorable visit

<Author>golfah01
<Content>Good Hotel My wife and I spent five nights at this hotel. On recommendation from friends we upgraded to a harbour view club room.The room was large with a king size bed. <Author>vmimartins
<Content>Great hotel - but location.... This is a great city hotel.Wonderful room, spotless, a free water bottle per person per day - really confortable. For us the location was not a problem, but it can be an issue. If you want to stay in the midlle of the action, this is not the place. To TsimTsaTui you can take the free shuttle from the hotel into the Peninsula hotel.Taxis are cheap - from TSt/Peninsula was about HK$30. Good breakfast buffet with plenty of asian food. Nearby the hotel, at Whampoa Gardens, there are restaurants and stores with plenty of choices.The roof top pool has great views but it closes at 8pm! I would stay here again and not hesitate to recommend.

<Author>mashap
<Content>Great hotel but weird staff Overall this hotel was great but we had some strange moments. I had splurged for the harbor view so when we arrived we got a room assigned to the 9th floor. I asked if we could be moved to a higher floor and the front desk had a weird reaction, almost like How dare you ask. Could be my imagination of course. My husband thought it was because we look quite young. So the concierge took us up to our room and when we walked in, it jus stank of smoke. We of course requested a non-smoking room and the room smelled like it was being used for that purpose solely. We didn't overreact just calmly said that there is not way we can stay here, and the concierge I think was embarrassed. He called down to the front desk and they immediately upgraded us to a club floor. A questions begs itself - why didn't they just upgrade us right away when I asked and instead tried to shove us in a smoking room? Weird. From there on things improved. The club floor must have had amenities but noone told us about them so we didn't use them. The buffet lunch was out of this world. Best ever. But the service was questionable. We kept asking the server to bring more coffee and he just seemed like it was a chore for him. Like he was surprised we wanted so much coffee. I don't see where he got the idea that he is supposed to judge how much coffee we drink.The room was nice and the view was quite nice but not as spectacular because it was blocked a bit by the hotel's left wing. We saw the harbour full view but not the cool skyscrapers. The last day there was a typhoon and we all got stuck at the hotel. It was surprisingly fun. We went for a harbor promenade during the eye of the storm passing over Hong Kong and it was super. Also the hotel is located three minute walk from the ferry that goes to Central station on Hong Kong island - very convenient. Our last night we went to the hotel's grill restaurant and had kobe beef. That was particularly outstanding. On top of a very nice meal, the restaurant gave us each a second glass of wine on the house. Overall great hotel and we would stay there again, I just don't really understand some of the staff attitude. Seems they were happier catering to an older crowd.

Short stroll to ferry to Central although it stops around 7pm. However a taxi from TSt/Peninsula was about HK$30 or so - nothing at all. Airport and station shuttle buses were fine but as soon as you discover the price of taxis....Really excellent breakfast buffet especially if you can get an inclusive rate. Staff were superb - we were greeted by Dilshan the doorman in person - somehow he knows your name. It is little touches that make it special. Lovely roof top pool and good gym/fitness faciliites.This is one hotel where I break the usual rule of location location location - becuase the location is actually entirely fine and the rest of the hotel makes up for any tiny shortcomings on location.I would not hesitate to recommend. And the photos are totally representative of the hotel and its rooms.

<Author>travellerfourlife
<Content>Very, very nice hotel The Harbour Plaza was splendid. The experience started at the airport, where they have their own info desk. They were able to double check the reservation and recommend transportation options to get into town. We wound up taking a taxi, which cost $300 HKD, about $40 US, but it was so much easier than any of the other option that it was worth it. Location is not perfect; the Harbour Plaza sits right on the waterfront in Hung Hom, a couple of miles east of Tsim Sha Tsui. Originally I thought this would be inconvenient. But there is a Star Ferry pier five minute walk from the hotel that runs to Central. The hotel offers a free shuttle to Tsim Sha Tsui, but we never had to use it. By then end of our stay, we were using taxis, which are so much easier than any other form of transit and are not that expensive. Also, Hung Hom/Whampoa turned out to be a pretty interesting area. It is largely residential, but there are many, many shops, restaurants, etc with in a ten minute walk of the hotel. Food and shopping were not a problem. It is a bit less energetic than Tsim Sha Tsui, and I missed the buzz, but it was nowhere near as isolated as I was afraid it would be.The rooms were perfect, very nice, large, fully equipped. I have stayed in nicer, but not by much. The lobby is absolutely stunning; it is in fact a favorite place for weddings in Hong Kong. And the hotel鈥檚 signature feature is a roof-top swimming pool that has a glass wall so that you can look out from the pool over Hong Kong Harbor from 21 floors up. Stunning. We did not eat in the hotel, but the food looked very good. Service was exceptional. Great concierge and bell staff. I whole heartedly recommend this hotel as a slightly quieter alternative to the chaos of Tsim Sha Tsui. Great value for the dollar.  
<Date>Aug 2, 2008

<Author>Tim_the_Taf
<Content>Could be good, but some issues Situated in Hung Hom on Kowloon, so a bit out of things. Bit of a pain in the evening; have to get a taxi into the main Kowloon area, or ferries to HK Island. Be aware that harbour view rooms have a harbour view, but not a view of the city. Hotel courtesy shuttle service was unreliable (if the bus was full, not another for 30 mins or an hour) so my advice is don't rely on it. Taxis are relatively cheap but take a dual language hotel card, there are lots more mainland Chinese there these days, and they speak little or no English.Rooms are pretty good, but we didn't have hot water for 2 days, and the second day had gritty brown water instead. Hotel apologised but no compensation offered. Considering we had 2 harbour view rooms this was unacceptable, and spoiled an otherwise Ok visit. Just highlighted the overall view on customer service: apologies but no real action or focus on the customer.Hotel food was generally good. Evening buffet was expensive but good and breakfast buffet is the usual international style buffet. Perfectly adequate, just make sure you don't pay a lot for it.Views from the roof top pool are sensational, worth a visit to see them.Beware of prices for electronics etc.; we did some research online whilst there and found we could get SLR cameras and equipment much cheaper in the UK than in HK.HK generally - found that since my last trip 10 years ago, language has become a problem; far fewer people spoke English, guess its the influx of mainland Chinese. Particularly bad on the local buses, and one driver in particular just simply ignored us. Also didn't feel safe there this time, especially in Aberdeen, so not sure I'd go again. Didn't help that my son's PSP was stolen out of his hand luggage at HK airport. Singapore feels a lot safer and is much easier to get around, so we'd stick to there as a stopover point in future.

<Author>Peter_Smallhill
<Content>Adequate for a night's rest I've stayed here several times on business trips. The most recent time, I booked a deluxe view room and got a small room with a view of high rises.Room was basic with a fairly hard bed, desk and straight chair, small TV with satellite channels. Bathroom had standard amenities and an excellent shower.No drinking water supplied in the room. You have to buy bottled water in the minibar.Soundproofing is not great - I heard a guy next door coughing during the night.The buffet restaurant near the lobby is good, but crowded and very noisy. Room service food is fair.Service is always friendly. The hotel caters mostly to mainland Chinese and other Asian travelers and has a lot of services they like. They provide a lot of in-room massage services and on previous visits I had calls in the evening asking whether I wanted a girl to come to my room. (This is common in China but not in Hong Kong.)Location is OK because taxis are available and the subway is nearby. You will need them because the immediate area offers nothing.Adequate for a night's rest, but nothing special.

<Author>rallton
<Content>Strange Payment Requirement The hotel is beautiful and the room was very comfortable. We booked a harbor view room but had only a very limited view of the harbor.If booking on the hotel web site, be aware that after booking the room, the hotel will send an email requiring you to send copies of your passport along with a copy of the front and back of your credit card and your signature. I was not comfortable sending this information due to identity theft concerns. I was charged a $15.00 cancellation fee by the hotel because I refused to send this information.I was able to book the room on Expedia for the same price without these unusual requirements.

<Author>dawnp61
<Content>Fantastic hotel Stayed here for two nights in May and absolutely loved it. HK is expensive in terms of hotels and this one provides the amazing buzz of that incomparable view to HK Island across the harbour as well as being affordable. Very little in HK will offer both those!Nice room, much larger than HK average. They don't have the 'wow' view of the famous HK skyline - they're on the wrong side of the building for that - but you still get a floor-to-ceiling view of the harbour with an always-changing vista of working boats, cruise ships and yachts. Very comfy beds and a large bathroom with rainforest shower and separate tub was also appreciated. All the room amenities were spot-on.The public areas - reception, bars, cafes and restaurants - do have the most stunning views of the city, especially at night over a drink or meal. It really has been designed to have the 'wow' factor in that sense. The open-air rooftop swimming pool does, too. Great spa facilities with massage, facials etc. Restaurant options were good and varied - Chinese, Japanese, a Grill and the wonderful alfresco Italian out by the promenade in front of the hotel. They're a bit pricey but in keeping with the standard of the hotel itself. There's no need to eat in the hotel in HK as it's a food capital of the world but if you do find yourself staying in on a cold, rainy night as we did, then you won't be disappointed.Staff were generally wonderfully helpful, efficient and friendly with one or two exceptions (unfortunately, the exceptions were highlighted due to the high standard of service from everyone else!).On the Kowloon side, the hotel's location is a little bit quieter than staying near the hub of the Nathan Road area but there is a free shuttle bus to the Star Ferry terminal and taxis are plentiful and very cheap. If you're planning on spending a lot of time in the shops, bars and clubs of Central and Wan Chai, then this place might seem too out of the way but, having visited HK several times now and tried hotels on the Island as well as Kowloon, I rate this as a fantastic alternative. I'll certainly be coming back here.

<Author>Doughballs
<Content>Loved it I spent alot of time on Tripadvisor trying to find the most suitable hotel for our trip to HK - the ones I really wanted to stay at were out of my price range, but the Harbour Plaza had received consistently good reviews both on Tripadvisor and other sites / magazines. Not knowing HK I did not know whether the location would be good or not, and when we first arrived I thought we had made the wrong choice as the hotel is outside the centre of Kowloon. I was wrong ! Although not central there is a Star Ferry almost in front of the hotel which runs every 20 minutes or so to HK island. And a free regular hotel shuttle which takes you to Kowloon central and back. Alternatively taxi is less than 拢2 to centre of Kowloon. So location was not a problem. Hotel is very good (only thing I really disliked was that the Air conditioning is on freezing in all the public areas..). Make sure you get a Harbour View room. Beautiful pool area on top of the hotel roof, but windy while we were there. Hotel bus shuttle from aiport to hotel is 130 HK USD per person. If there are 2 of you it is hardly more expensive (and less hassle) to get a taxi which is 280-300 HK USD.A lovely hotel that I would stay at again, and very good value.

<Author>Marina26
<Content>A good hotel for a first timer This was my first time in Hong Kong and I booked this hotel based on the very favourable reviews on Trip Advisor.The reviews were largely accurate. The hotel is slightly out of the centre but there is a very good and efficient shuttle bus that takes you from the hotel and drops you off right outside the Pen. The driver normally puts his foot down and so this takes about 10 minutes. If you miss the last shuttle bus in the evening, you can jump into one of the red Hong Kong taxi cabs which are very cheap. The lobby of the hotel is very bright and has wonderful views of Hong Kong Island. We didn't fancy the buffet breakfast in the morning and so we were going to a coffee shop around the corner every day for coffee and a croissant. Our room was on the 18th floor and it was fine apart from the fact that the toilet didn't flush properly on arrival but that was soon sorted out. I must admit, I didn't find the reception / concierge staff particularly helpful especially when I was trying to book some trips and tours. Nevertheless, if this is your first time in Hong Kong and you want to stay somewhere relatively clean and cheap, then the Harbour Plaza is the place for you.

<Author>oak74
<Content>Excellent base in Hong Kong We were looking for a base to explore Hong Kong with our 2 young children and booked the HP after reading earlier reviewers comments which by and large were pretty close to the mark in terms of our experience. We booked an Ocean Suite for the four of us and the Hotel had no problem putting in two additional roll away beds (HK400++ ea) for the children in the lounge/kitchenette room. The view of Victoria Harbour provided a spectacular backdrop with everything from ocean liners to Chinese junks literally sailing past the windows but it is worth noting that the hotel's location means that you will only get a glimpse of the 8pm light show from the hotel. However as mentioned in earlier reviews the location, whilst not right in the middle of downtown, is still really quite good as the cross harbour ferry to Central is virtually at the doorstep, taxis are always at the door and are extremely cheap (our most expensive trip was from the base of the peak tram on HK island back to the hotel - HK90.00 including tolls, most other trips were HK30-50) and the hotels shuttle bus provides a terrific half hourly service to TST which will drop you off in the best possible spot to see the show. The accommodation and service was of the standard you would expect for this level of hotel and the staff were professional and courteous.The roof top pool has an amazing view of the HK skyline.There are plenty of shops, restaurants etc just a short stroll from the hotel including banks and supermarkets etc.The only slight criticism we could make is that the breakfast buffet, whilst adequate, is probably not quite up to the mark when compared against similar standard hotels we have stayed in, in other parts of Asia. We ended up going to local coffee shops/cafes instead - offering an easy breakfast alternative.In summary, were we satisfied -yes, and we would probably happily consider staying there again next time.

<Author>ochief19
<Content>Mediocre at Best We booked this hotel while we were staying here on vacation for 10 days and found the following problems-overly expensive decent at best 25 US dollar breakfast buffet, also it closes at 11 and they will let you in at 10:55 and pack up the food 5 minutes later which happened to us-20 US dollars per day for internet access that is terribly slow, whereas roughly 80% of hotels in hong kong (many of them with much cheaper rates) offer free high speed access-10 US dollar food-reheating charge, gave them my Morton's prime rib that was medium rare and they brought it back well done, though this may seem terribly picky they asked me twice how they should do it and i said i just want it warmed, not re-cooked-Terrible room cleaning, they leave empty bottles all over the place, forgot to leave towels twice, stains on bed and sheets, what looks to be a nice blood stain on the marble bathroom floor and the toilet doesnt flush properly-TV is older than i am, doesnt work, no channel selection, tough to turn on, cannot change volume etc...-Location is not as central as they make it seem, though in a harbour, it is not even close to being the main harbour with the famous star ferry and beautiful shopping centers. Not a shopping center, MTR, Ferry, Nightlife, good restaurants or anything else within a 30 minute walk, or ten minute taxi. Overall the room and Hotel was OK, the lobby is beautiful, room size (for hong kong) is great and staff are fairly pleasant. For all the hype definately not worth it. Next time i come I would spend an extra 50 dollars a night to stay in a more elite hotel, that this one tries to be like.

<Author>WorldwidePrincess
<Content>Great hotel in Whampoa Gardens This is a good value, excellent hotel in a gorgeous setting on the harbour, and I've stayed here twice. You walk in and there are floor to ceiling windows along the water, and that's your breakfast view too. The location is good for a little walk along the harbour, and there's a lot around the hotel, including the ferry to Wan Chai (and Central too maybe?). The hotel is not walking distance to Kowloon, however. It is also not on a subway or train line. Apart from the ferry (which doesn't run past early evening), you have to rely on taxis or the hotel shuttle bus. If you can handle that, it's a great choice. Lately I've been staying at the sister hotel, Harbour Plaza Metropolis, which is at Hung Hom Station, to be closer to Kowloon and the station, but I miss the water there...Tip: Print off the address in Chinese for taxi drivers. Because of the name of the hotel, I have found myself heading toward Hong Kong Island because the taxi driver just assumed it was on the island because of the name.

<Author>foggysam
<Content>Wonderful Harbour Plaza On our way from Australia to Europe we decided to give our little kids a break and stay a few nights in Hong Kong to interrupt the trip. Decided on the Harbour Plaza based on different reviews found here and elsewhere.The Harbour Plaza was fantastic. From the moment we booked our room until they dropped us back off at the airport, the customer service and hospitality were among the best we have ever experienced.Our room was fairly spacious with a great view and very well equipped. All amenities we needed were available on-site. We decided to book a club room, which came with the added benefits of a separate check-in / concierge desk as well as the club lounge / business centre, which came in very handy.We arranged a hotel pick-up at the airport which was very simple with a hotel desk in the arrivals hall of the airport.The hotel is in Kowloon, which is out of the centre but close enough to get there quickly either by hotel bus, taxi or by ferry.We would definitely recommend this hotel very highly and hope to stay there again soon.

<Content>Excellent Hotel! <Author>ClaireeTurnip
<Content>The best hotel in Hong Kong We bkd the HP after reading previous reviews and we were not disappointed. Pre stay, the hotel booked seats for us on the Airport Shuttle Coach on arrival in HK Airport and this made the end of our long journey very comfortable. The location of the hotel is ideal, it's on the waterfront overlooking Victoria Harbour and there's a lovely walkway way directly in front of the hotel which is ideal for a post breakfast or pre dinner stroll. We arrived at the hotel late afternoon after a long flight and were greeted by extremely professional, friendly and courteous staff. One of the doormen actually remembered my name for the duration of our 3 night stay. Our harbour view room was spacious, very comfortable and just as expected from a 5* hotel. The breakfast buffet was lovely, albeit, the waiters don't leave coffee pots on your table and you have to keep asking for refills (a very minor criticism). We had the dinner buffet twice as to be honest there isn't that much directly around the hotel and again the choice and quality were very good. There is a free hourly shuttle bus into the centre of Kowloon from the hotel as it's just too far to walk. The hotel is an ideal base for seeing the sites of HK as it's away from all the hussle  bussle and we will definately stay at the HP next time we visit HK.

<Author>sussexholidayholic
<Content>WOW what an entrance I stayed at this hotel 15th and 16th March 2008 prior to a cruise down to Vietnam. When we drove up to the main entrance it reminded me of the glitz of Las Vegas. It was simply stunning. Checking in was very smooth at the spacious, elegant reception area and the superior harbour view room on the 11th floor had beautiful views of the harbour from the large panoramic windows. The bathroom was huge however the placement of the loo was somewhat of an after thought!. There were always staff on hand at reception to carry luggage, open doors and order taxis and they were always very polite. The food in the Harbour Grill Restaurant was very good but a little pricey, mainly due to the high cost of wine in general, in Hong Kong. I would agree that the location is some what a little way out of the happening part of the city but it was refreshing to be able to stroll out on the promenade either before or after dinner and enjoy a drink at the Waterfront bar (which has an extended happy hour most evenings). The hotel does operate an excellent free shuttle bus to and from the main area and a star ferry is on the door step, so all in all you have just about the best combination you could want. I would return without any hesitation and would strongly recommend this hotel to any of my friends.

<Author>bmarsh
<Content>A Good Find If this is your first time to Hong Kong or if you are a leisure traveler then this hotel is probably a pretty good bet for you. If you have travelled to Hong Kong and stayed previously in any of the major hotels then you will notice that the service here whilst excellent compared to elsewhere in the world, is just not as slick and sharp and does not quite meet the standard of Hong Kong鈥檚 many other better known hotels. I have stayed in most of the well know hotels in Hong Kong so I guess I may expect a lot.That said, the rate I paid was below current rates for the better known hotels and as housekeeping, choice of food and all other things met the usual superb Hong Kong standards, it was a pretty good deal.The location may or may not be a problem. Located about 1 hour walk from the main shopping areas around Nathan road (walking not suggested as busy flyovers in the way) the hotel operates a quick and frequent free bus shuttle service to the shopping area and the airport express station. Taxi鈥檚 are also easy to find and cheap in Hong Kong. In fact although the hotel is in a residential area it has a greater feeling of space than is usual in Hong Kong.The harbor view from the hotel or the walk way outside is arguably better than from the better know harbour side hotels as you get a much better perspective from the distance. If you are on business and visiting the exhibition centre in Wan Chai (Honk Kong Island) this may not be an obvious hotel to stay. However, the hotel is 4 minutes walk from the Hung Hom star ferry terminal to Wan Chai and Central and is probably one of the easiest Kowloon hotels to reach the island from. In fact for an alternative and more pleasant way to reach the main shopping areas of Kowloon from the hotel, it is no big deal if you have the time (and costs less than HK$10) to take a ferry to Wan Chai and then from Wan Chai back to Kowloon and the main star ferry terminal/shopping area.Would I stay here again, probably.

<Author>H2OTGP
<Content>Harbour Plaza Paradise My wife and I recently spent 3 nights at the Harbour Plaza on our way to Thailand and whilst the weather was unkind to us the hotel certainly made up for it. I booked direct with the hotel via it's website back in September and at the time it was the cheapest way with no upfront payment. About 3 weeks before leaving I saw a cheaper package offered and when I contacted the hotel and explained they were more than happy to match the price! We booked a Harbour Club Harbour view room and we were very pleased with it.The extra cost of the club room is well worth it as it includes Breakfast either in the Club lounge or downstairs in the main breakfast area. ( Two breakfasts alone are nearly as much as the club supplement! ) You then have the advantage of fast track check in and out, Tea  coffee throughout the day and a splendid  Afternoon Tea  from 3 till 6. Then from 6 till 8 you can help your self to pre dinner snacks, wine and beer. The staff were all very helpful and polite and the maid service was twice a day and very proffesional.We did not use the hotel restaurants as they were fairly expensive although we did order room service on our first night as we arrived quite late. The Fish and chips were probably the best we had tasted for quite some time and the cost very reasonable.We used the hotel limo for our airport transfers and whilst a bit more expensive than the mini bus it is a little bit special to be whisked along in a top of the range S class Mercedes with the driver pointing out all the points of interest along the way ( Cost $550HK one way or $1050HK return )As mentioned previously the location is a bit out of the way but that is a bonus to be honest so don't let that put you off. I can honestly say that if I return to HK in the future it will be to stay at the Harbour Plaza.

<Content>A good 5 Star Hotel We had booked two rooms on the club floor, check in is in the club lounge on the 20th floor. The rooms were a good size, furnished to a good standard and clean. A nice touch was a set of personalised stationary put in the room on our arrival, Internet access was free. The lounge is comfort and a pleasant place to relax. The hotel provides a bus every half hour to Nathan Road, which was a great as it rained the entire time we were there. The locals told us the hotel is in a very safe part of Kowloon, and was ok to go out in the evening. .Apart from the weather which ruined the time we had in Hong Kong, The hotels roof top pool would be great in good weather as it overlooks the harbour. <Author>jeffwin1668
<Content>Wonderful Stay at the Harbour Plaza We stayed at this hotel for 12 nights, spending Christmas  New Year in Hong Kong. We booked 2 harbour view rooms and the hotel arranged inter-connecting rooms that provided more moving space as a whole. Here's a more detail review.Location:Granted this hotel is not smack in the middle of everything (i.e. MTR, shopping, Nathan Rd etc..) but it is in a very nice upscale neighbourhood with shopping nearby and waterfront area with great views of the harbour. We prefer retreating to this area especially after a long day venturing out to sightsee and being in other crowded areas all day long. Lobby:The front area and lobby looks grand and the staircase is decorated practically everyday with different wedding parties (there were weddings going on everyday that we were there). Front desk staff was efficient and polite but what stood out was one of the door man who remembered my name since the day we go there. Every time he opened the door for us, he鈥檒l mention my name which makes you feel special. It鈥檚 little things like that stands out and you鈥檒l remember this. Room:The room is large for Hong Kong standard. We booked a harbour view and really enjoyed the view and seeing ships of all sizes coming and going. My 3 yr old liked the inter-connecting rooms for us and my parents as he can run around in both rooms without going outside into the hallway. The only regret was the room did not face the main harbour where the festival of lights (Christmas lights on buildings) and the fireworks display were held on New Year鈥檚 Eve. Not sure if any rooms in the hotel do face that direction or maybe for the more expensive suites only. However, I do know that for hotels that face directly at the main harbour where you can see everything will cost a lot more than the Harbour Plaza and rooms are likely to be smaller as well. The d茅cor of the room is standard and the furnishing is also standard. It also shows some wear and tear in a few places but overall it was clean and in good shape. Service:Service (House keeping) is on and off meaning sometimes is good and sometimes not so good. For a hotel rated as 5 stars, service should be top notched but sometimes this is not the case. Nothing major but little things that get forgotten (more than once) should not occur for a 5 star hotel. For example, since our son shares the room with us, we asked for an extra set of towels for him but this is forgotten once every few days. There was also a small fruit platter which we were told at first it would be replenished everyday but when it didn鈥檛, we asked again and we were then told this was only for the 1st night but since we asked, they would replenish it again and this occurred for another 2 days but then stopped. We didn鈥檛 bother to ask anymore as we can buy our own fruit at the local supermarket nearby. In general, staff was polite and helpful.Transportation:Hotel provides a small shuttle bus to TST but gets filled up quickly but will not drive off until the schedule time even if the bus is already full. They should at least increase this service especially for peak periods. Taxis are available and fairly cheap compared to North America and you can also walk to the pier a few minutes away to take the ferry across to Hong Kong Island. I like this way the best. However, since the ferry stops running after 8pm, if you are returning late, you鈥檒l have to rely on other means of transportation.Restaurants:We didn鈥檛 try the hotel restaurants as we eat out most of the time but we did have drinks at the hotel lounge late in the evening. The buffet looks good and I really wanted to try it but never got around to it. There are also many restaurants around the area and the prices are obviously a lot cheaper than at the hotel. Since we speak the local language, there鈥檚 no problem for us but even for tourist that doesn鈥檛 speak Cantonese, it shouldn鈥檛 be difficult as most restaurants there have menus in both Chinese  English language.Conclusion:Overall, this is a good hotel and I wouldn鈥檛 hesitate to recommend this. You will not regret by picking this hotel. Hope this helps鈥?/p>

<Author>Red1973
<Content>A Brilliant Hotel This is a superb hotel from a Tourist perspective. The hotel is stunning being right on the waters edge looking across the harbour towards Hong Kong Island. The rooms are beautifully appointed (I had a Harbour View Room and the view was stunning) and the gym, pool and other facilities were excellent. The staff were also helpful and pleasant and it was a joy to stay here. It is a 5 minute walk to the Star Ferry Terminal for the 10 minute Ferry Ride to Central or Wan Chai on Hong Kong Island. In addition, the hotel runs a courtesy bus to and from Tsim Sha Tsui in Kowloon giving you easy access to this part of town. Taxis are also plentiful and good value for money. The area right outside the hotel is worth not dismissing as there are numerous good value restaurants here as well as Internet cafes where the use of the internet will cost you the price of a coffee. Tip - Ensure you get the hotel to write down the name of the hotel in cantonese for the taxis as there are 3 other hotels of the same name. A brilliant hotel - Just go!

<Author>irishnz
<Content>Generally an Excellent Hotel I enjoyed my stay at the Harbour Plaza Hong Kong - over the new year period. Certainly a popular hotel - we were there 6 days and each day there was a wedding! It was great to see the grand staircase get decorated each day. We had a lovely corner room with great views over the harbour (or look below and see the locals doing tai chi each day). Lovely outdoor pool area at the top of the hotel with great views.Staff were great, very friendly and attentive. The hotel was spotless. Food - one meal through room service was great, the other was awful. The breakfast buffet had a fantastic range and the food was great, though the usual hotel prices. The hotel wasn't quite in the centre so we did use the free shuttle frequently. Several times it was full but taxis were very cheap, so not an issue. It is worth checking out the timetable for the nearby ferry as it is only a few mins away and quick and easy to get to Hong Kong Island. We found the shuttle from the airport to the hotel was a bit lengthly - waiting for the next one to depart. Also, we were the last hotel for drop offs, so from arriving at airport, took almost 2 hours to reach hotel. Leaving was fine, very efficient. Definitely agree with other reviews about getting an octopus card at the airport, then you can use all the transport including star ferry. Overall, would recommend the hotel, we enjoyed our stay and I would return.

<Author>Warks
<Content>Excellent hotel, enjoyed our stay at the Harbour Plaza Just returned from spending New Year in Hong Kong, staying at the Harbour Plaza. It would be difficult to find fault with this hotel, beautiful views and all the staff were polite and helpful. We took the airport express to Kowloon and then the free shuttle bus to the hotel, all well sign posted and no waiting, from landing to reaching our room took about 90 minutes. It is worth buying an Octopus Card at the airport, public transport in Hong Kong is very easy to use and cheap, we toured Hong Kong Island, took the Peak Tram and the ferries to outlying islands, used the metro and over 5 days it cost us 拢15. On arriving at the hotel the check in process was smooth and we were upgraded to Harbour Club Class on the 19th floor, do pay a little extra for the harbour view, this certainly made our stay. A ferry pier is 5 minutes from the hotel and you can go to both Central and Wan Chai from here, the only drawback is that these routes stop running about 8pm. This did not cause problems as the hotel runs a free shuttle service ( but do get to it early to get a seat) or public bus No 6 runs past the hotel, if all else fails it is a 25minute walk along the harbour front from the middle of Kowloon. For us the position of this hotel was not a problem, the quality, service, view and price were well worth any slight inconvenience. Loved Hong Kong and would stay at the Harbour Plaza again.

<Author>ProfSue
<Content>Wonderful hotel This is a wonderful hotel on the Kowloon side with spectacular views of the Hong Kong skyline IF you get the right room; ask for a harbor view room, then if you don't get a room with enough view of the skyline go back to the desk and ask for another one. We had to take a smoking room to get a great view, but the room didn't smell of smoke, and we only caught a whiff of smoke in the hall a couple of times. The only disadvantage is that it's not centrally located, however there is a bus every half hour to downtown, and from there it's an easy walk to the Star Ferry, several museums, and lots of shopping. Also, the free bus to/from the airport train comes by every half hour.The hotel restaurants are expensive, as hotel restaurants are, but there are a number of restaurants within a few blocks. The buffet breakfast is amazing but costs around US$35, and we weren't lucky enough to get the free upgrade as some other reviewers have reported.This is the second time I've stayed here and will again.

<Author>Jimsydney
<Content>Another happy camper Based on previous reviews of this hotel we booked two rooms - one of our children and one for my wife and myself and stayed for 9 nights during December 2007 . The reviews were spot on and we all had a great time at a hotel that certainly looks after its customers. It probably isn't worth repeating a lot of what has been covered in previous posts except to say:1. Yes the hotel is a bit further out but its near the ferry, the hotel offers a free bus ride into the city at half hour intervals, and in any event the taxi ride from the centre of the city was only HK$30. My wife loved the location near a couple of parks where she joined in the morning tai chi rituals (I went swimming on the rooftop!)2. Our deal included breakfast at the 'club' on level 19 I think. This was a very well set out buffet catering for about 30/40 people but it was rarely more than half full. The food and service was fantastic - well worth it.2. Get an octupus card. public transport is quick, regular and easy to use - even to out of the way locations like the wetlands - new territories. This card is a debit card with the cost of the trip being taken out of the pre paid balance. The entrance to the stations, buses etc all have readers - just swipe your card to have the cost of the trip deducted - usually only HK$4/$5. We had a great time in Hong Kong and very glad we chose the Plaza - thanks to all previous reviewers!

<Author>steviec1211
<Content>Great value for money Stayed for 3 nights in this impressive hotel which anywhere else would merit 5 stars. Large lobby/check in area with a huge marble staircase and fountain. Very helpful staff and no delays checking in or out. The room was a superior room with views out over the harbour. (Fantastic) It was large with a huge king size bed and plenty of room to move around. The bathroom was also huge and both were very clean and comfortable. There are a choice of restaurants in the hotel plus an excellent small coffee shop. The choice and quality of food is extensive, especially in the downstairs buffet restaurant, but it is a little on the expensive side. I was concerned about the location as it is a bit away from the action in downtown Kowloon but I need not have worried as there is a free shuttle bus every half hour to Nathan road and the Star Ferry, plus the other ferry over to Hong Kong Island is only a five minute walk away. There is also a lovely roof top pool and Fitness room on the top of the Hotel with fantastic views over the city. Overall this place is excellent value for money offering a standard of comfort and service that you would pay at least three times as much for in central Kowloon or on the island. I would recommend it to anyone.

<Author>geggs
<Content>Just go W stayed for 5 nights in October. The airport was easy to navigate with friendly and helpful staff ( the security staff put to shame the third world arrangements at Heathrow). One tip, make sure you collect the excellent local guide to HK, freely available in the airport. It contains all of the tourist destinations in chinese, necessary as most taxi drivers don't speak english.We used a prebooked coach transfer to the hotel. We didn't want to carry luggage across HK with our 10 month old. The system worked well and the journey (45 minutes) was enjoyable.The hotel is stunning. We had a superior room with a harbour view on the 17th floor. Spacious, well fitted and a large marble bathroom. Fabulour views from the room and indeed the entire hotel. The swimming pool is on the roof on the 22nd floor. Even if you don't swim, just go for the views, particularly at night. The pool closes at 8pm.We didn't eat in the hotel. Five minutes walk away is Whampoa Gardens with a separate block called the Gourmet Place. It has around 30 restaurants catering for all budgets and tastes, from dim sum to ox penis. And no, we didn't.As well documented by previous correspondents, the hotel is in the affluent end of Hung Hom and away from the tat of south Nathan Road. We welcomed this. It is a break from the assault on your senses which is HK, but never far - a 5 minute walk, to the Hung Hom ferry terminal with direct ferries to North Point and Central.Excellent walks fom the hotel, particularly east along the waterfront. You can literally walk for miles if you want. Very safe and evocative at night.You expect 5 star bar prices at 5 star hotels, even in cheap HK, but the Waterfront Bar offers happy hour between 5-8.30pm which brings a cocktail or a pint of Stella to around 拢2. Not bad by any standards. The views from the bar are phenominal, arrive early for a front row table. But feel sorry for the entertainers who have to play inside to empty tables because everyone wants to sit outside. Don't worry, there's no karaoke.From check in to check out, the staff and Concierge were first class. It makes me so unhappy with what passes for service in British hotels.I am quite sure that all of the 5 star hotels offer great service and facilities, but don't be at all put off by the hotel location, it's an asset.  
<Date>Oct 26, 2007

<Author>hobbitsky
<Content>Beautiful location and hotel this hotel is in a lovely area with nice restaurants in the hotel or around. The room we had overlooking the courtyard was spaceous and very clean. You can book a harbour view room but as we were either in the rooftop pool which overlooks the harbour or walking the area felt it wasn't worth the extra expense. The boardwalk area also overlooks the harbour and is quite beautiful especially at night. A ferry is only a few steps away. The free shuttle service is OK but does not go to the ladies markets etc so you have to find your own way. Taxi's are very cheap but make sure you have someone write your destination point and take the hotel address in Chinese as many do not speak english. The shuttle does however take you to Kowloon Station where they book you in for your flight and take your luggage and then you can take the express train to the airport. Very easy but leave plenty of time. From leaving the hotel till arriving at the gate of departure at the airport it took 4 hours. We had a transfer booked on our arrival and found this very messy as you have to walk a long way to reach the buses with your luggage. the train option was quicker as once you collect your luggage on arrival you just walk straight to the train just outside that area and hop on the train to Kowloon Station which is about a 20 minute ride and they have free shuttles to most hotels there. If however, your hotel is not amongst the free shuttles again a taxi is a very cheap mode of transport.

<Author>Zowie_F
<Content>Great Hotel with fantastic views Very good hotel with a roof top pool and terrace which is lovely. Our very nice, spacious room was on 17th flr overlooking the harbour so we had great view. When we arrived we were on the 9th flr with a less good view - we asked to be moved and it wasn't a problem for the very friendly staff at all.A couple of reviews have mentioned the location of this hotel. It is out of the main area but the transport links to / from the hotel are very good so we didn't find it a problem at all. The Star ferry to 'Central' and 'North Point' on Hong Kong Island is in front of the hotel and the hotel provides a free shuttle bus to Tsim Sha Tsui every 1/2 hr (takes less than 10 mins). We were only in HK for 2 days and the location was fine.One tip - if you arrive at HK airport - get the Airport Express train to Kowloon Train Station and then get the free transfer bus from the front of the station (one level up) which takes you straight to the hotel. Whole trip is less than an hr.

<Author>MonikafromSurrey
<Content>Impressive !! My husband and I stayed here for 3 nights in early September, on our way to Samui, Thailand. We stayed in a Club Harbourview Room on the 19th floor and liked it. The room looked smaller than on the hotel's website and the bathroom was quite dated. However, the view over the Victoria Harbour was as good as promised. We used the Club Lounge a couple of times and were satisfied with the choice of snacks and food at breakfast. However, the choice of drinks was rather limited and we had to ask specially for mineral water. They brought us 2 little bottles on the first occasion but afterwards only served it in a tiny glass (one at a time). Really strange. The hotel offers a complimentary shuttle bus service to the Airport Express station and a city centre in Kowloon. It was handy when we wanted to go shopping and move around the area. The Concierge Desk had few tours to offer and helped us to book a last minute trip to Lantau Island. Good choice. One evening we had drinks and sat outside at the Waterfront Bar. It was lovely and we even got tempted with some appetizers in the end. We didn't regret it. Overall, it's an impressive hotel but we would be tempted to try a different one next time, for example Shangri-La in Kowloon.

<Author>Hammers
<Content>Ideal for a stop over in Hong Kong My wife and I stayed at the Harbour Plaza as a stop over on our way home from New Zealand. The hotel met all our requirements which was mainly somewhere to relax after 5 weeks travelling; and we were not disappointed with our choice. The hotel is positioned away from the main hassle in a quieter part of Kowloon. An early morning swim (the pool is on the 22nd floor) sets you up for a days exploration. There is a local ferry terminal, very close by, which provides a fascinating journey to Hong Kong Island from where all the main tourist attractions can be visited. If you require to travel into Kowloon the hotel provides a free shuttle bus with conveniently placed drop off points. Taxi's are a way of life and therefore are very reasonable should you require another part of town. After a days sightseeing we returned to the hotel for the evening Happy Hour (more than welcome when the temperature exceeds 33 C) and the main restaurants provided an adequate selection of meals if you decided to stay local for the evening. Alas 4 days is a very small time in Hong Kong but we will return to both Hong Kong and the Harbour Plaza.

My family (husband, sister and parents) and I had been visiting relatives in New Zealand and decided to have a few nights in Hong Kong on the way back to England. <Author>DannyDLondon
<Content>Fantastic hotel - couldn't fault it I don't often give a hotel five stars, so coming from me this is high praise indeed.The experience was faultless and the quality excellent.We booked a club room on the 18th floor with harbour views, and it was well worth the upgrade. Absolutely stunning views, and great room. Don't miss the pool on the roof with more harbour views and the breakfast buffet which was excellent.Things to bear in mind:- This hotel is on the Kowloon side, which isn't really a problem, because transportation to the Hong Kong side is great, but you should be aware in case you want to room in the absolute centre.- If you are continuing your journey into the mainland from here, it makes sense to use Shenzhen airport because flights from here to other Chinese cities are much cheaper than HK airport - because they are considered domestic. There are ferries from Kowloon to Shenzhen (roughly 1 hour), but our taxi driver advised us that there is a new road from Hong Kong to Shenzhen, which is much quicker and easier to use (opened 2 weeks ago). Unfortunately for us, we already had the ferry booked, but it was a pleasant experience, and Chinese immigration took minutes on the Shenzhen side.

<Author>t16tomcat
<Content>Very recommendable hotel This is a nice modern hotel, with a good choice of restaurants and a good view, if you get a harbour view room.The place is modern and quite grand, plenty of marble and wide, light corridors. It would be an ideal business hotel.We went there as the first port of call for our honeymoon, and booked a Harbour Club room, you get a personal registration area, afternoon tea, evening buffet and private breakfast area and it is well worth taking advantage of and you are made very welcome. Breakfast and evening buffets are well worth doing.We did not however realise that it is quite a long way round the harbour and is not within walking distance of the famous hotels near the star ferry terminal. It is within the Hung Hom district. This meant that other than the hotels own restaurants, five if I remember, there is not much else unless you take a taxi ride. The Japanese Robatayaki restaurant is very good as is their own Chinese 鈥?Hoi Yat Heen, but both are quite expensive. The Waterfront bar is more reasonably priced for both food and drinks. There is a ferry terminus just outside so you can quickly get to the Hong Kong island ferry terminal in about 10 minutes and as taxis are so cheap and plenty full in Hong Kong access to other parts of the city is easy. One final thought, we went at the beginning of August 07, not a good time for a tourist as it is in Typhoon season and very hot and humid. The rooftop swimming pool is a great feature, but we were unable to use it, as with a typhoon warning in the area (only a grade 1, they go up to 10 !) they closed it for fear of lightning strikes.Overall a good tourist hotel, great features and as long as your mind is not set on a Tsim Shat Sui area hotel on the harbour front. a great one that is not too expensive. Finally, we booked through Asiarooms.com who offer some great deals and a easy to work with, however do not expect an immediate response as they are an agent. It takes 24 - 48 hrs and they debit your credit card before booking and the hotel is not always available.

<Author>World_Cup_Wanderer
<Content>Fantastic Harbour Views We chose this hotel for its value and views of the harbour, and we were not disappointed in any way. The views of the harbour are just fantastic. Note that we did book a harbourside room.The comfort and amenities at the hotel lived up to expectations. Everything that one expected was available and easily accessible.One thing to be aware of with this hotel is that it is a little out of the way from rail stations - and should not be confused with the like named Harbour Plaza Metropolis nearby (sister hotel). However, the hotel is located close to the Hung Hom star ferry terminal, and this provides easy and convenient transport access to the rest of HKs transportation systems. We pretty well used the ferry each day to start and end our outings, and linked up with the subway system from HK central.There are nice restuarants with outdoor dining within the hotel precinct, and these generally have a wonderful outlook over the harbour. For those who like to relax with a view, it is hard to top the pool deck on the roof, wihich has fantastic views of the harbour and the benefit of cooling breezes as one takes in the view - day or night.

<Author>joozy1
<Content>Fantastic hotel - especially the staff I've been meaning to write a review of the Harbour Plaza ever since we've returned from Hong Kong in mid-June but have been terribly lazy. However, the last two reviews have prompted me to offer a defence of the Harbour Plaza staff.To start with the basics, the Harbour Plaza is a fantastic hotel. The views from the rooms on the Harbour side are breath-taking, the decor is very good, the roof-top pool is brilliantly scary and the rooms are sizeable and comfy.What really made the Harbour Plaza stand out, though, was the service my girlfriend and I received on the final day of our holiday. Unfortunately, my girlfriend took ill during our final night at the Harbour Plaza. Eventually, she was so ill that I had to phone the duty manager and request a doctor. This was arranged very quickly and the doctor told us that my girlfriend would have to go to the hospital.Having made it to the hospital, my girlfriend had to undergo a number of tests and I realised that we would not be able to check out of the hotel on time. I then phoned the hotel to explain this, fully expecting that I'd have to pay something extra for late check-out - after all, this is a big bad hotel company isn't it?In actual fact, they couldn't have been more helpful. They told me that we could keep the room as long as was necessary for no extra cost. Thankfully, my girlfriend was discharged at approximately 5pm (with a small medicine cabinet's worth of drugs and a diagnosis - she'll live but she might need an op) and we made our way back to the Harbour Plaza. On our return, the staff could not have been more concerned or helpful. They all deserve immense credit - but special thanks must go to the superb duty manager.We eventually checked out at around 9pm and caught our flight back home at midnight. Thankfully, the sleeping pills that the hospital had gave my girlfriend ensured that she slept for approximately 10hours of the 12 hour flight.Now we just have to try and deal with the NHS..... anyone have a link to NHSAdvisor.com???

<Author>Travelscan
<Content>Check you bill and don't use the phone! For a five star hotel this is good value. We had a great room on the 16th floor overlooking the harbour. The room was a good size with comfortable beds and all the usual fittings - bar fridge, safe, iron, hairdryer etc. The general tone of the hotel was high class with lots of marble and gold chandeliers. \The buffet breakfast is good but get there early as not much is left by the 10 o'clock closing time. The Promenade Resturant buffet dinner is great value with unlimited softdrink, wine and beer for an extra $HK68. Book early as it is very popular with the locals.Check your bill carefully when departing as we were charged twice for breakfast. Also beware of the hotel telephone system. In Hong Kong local calls are free but this hotel charges $HK6 per call from your room. Also do not use a phone card with an 800 freecall number as they charge $HK30 per call onto your bill. Go down to the lobby and use the public phones for $HK1 a call. Fair value, nice decor, great views but check your bill and don't use the phones.

<Author>wanchaiSydney
<Content>Star staff member was the Sikh doorman, Panni ! Just returned from a six night stay at the Harbour Plaza Hong Kong with my two daughters 12 and 16. First impressions were good, luxurious feel about the place, crystal chandeliers, beautiful harbourfront location, extensive use of marble etc. On arrival, we were shown to our room which was supposed to be a deluxe harbour view room on club level with three beds. We found a very cramped corner room with only two beds and a slight glimpse of water between two buildings and no extra bed nor room to put one in there. Three people would have been very cramped in this room ! I immediately returned to reception to complain (coincidentally, I had seen mention of this practice on previous reviews of this hotel of them trying to palm people off with inferior rooms so, I was already alerted to this possibility)After lengthy argument with the staff who insisted we had the correct room for our booking we were finally shown to the room we should have had in the first place which was a fairly spacious room (by HK standards) on the 16th floor with a third bed already in place. The view was fabulous with a spectacular view of Victoria Harbour.My second daughter was to sleep on a rollaway bed and after one night she complained of back pain. The bed was very uncomfortable and the springs were poking through onto the mattress. We decided to ask for this bed to be removed in order to provide more floor space in the room and she would share a king single bed with me which was not entirely satisfactory but better than suffering from back pain. So, after paying extra for a rollaway bed my daughter and I had to share the king single which was also actually quite uncomfortable with lumpy parts and springs evident in some places. Not what one would expect from a 5 Star hotel. We were also challenged twice on why we had asked for the rollaway bed to be removed and told that we would still have to pay for it as it had been requested by us. All unecessary stress and hassle I could have done without. Also ,despite displaying the 'do not disturb' sign on our door the room maids still knocked and asked us if we needed our room making up that day or not.Overall, I liked the hotel and its facilites and location, some of the staff were great, especially concierge and door staff but, I don't know whether it was the five star experience I expected and it certainly wasn't hassle free ! I would have second thoughts about staying there again.

<Author>laurawellcoolstuff
<Content>better than the first time :) I have just returned back from my second stay at Harbour Plaza HK, and it was just as good/ if not better than my first stay.The hotel staff,bell boy, door men, and concierce are helpful from the second you arrive (I felt way too common to have the door held open for me each time we entered or left the building) but everyone is so welcoming and friendly. It really is a good impression that sticks in your mind.I previously emailed the hotel to request a room on a high floor. Upon arrival, I was so pleased to find we had been placed in a spacious harbour view room on the 17th floor (the club floor) which had 2 king beds. Wow!As nice as the room was, I couldn't wait to go to the pool. The power shower feels wonderful after a longhaul flight, but the bath is large aswell. Yes, the pool is not particularly gigantic, but it's enough to do a few lengths, and relax in the jacuzzi section. The view is far too magnificent to worry about the size of pool. If you don't fancy a swim, you can relax on one of the many sunlounger and enjoy a drink or meal. The corner cafe, Whampoa lounge, and harbour front terrace are a pleasure to eat at. Granted it's more pricey than eating outside the hotel, but the delicious and quick food, and the staff's welcoming and charm are worth the extra price.As everyone else has mentioned, there are hundreds of cheap dining options around the whampoa area.There is an excellent cafe/bar alongside the harbour next to the Hung Hom ferry terminal. They serve cheap street food, sandwiches, snacks, and it is a good spot to people watch. The surrounding area is filled with interesting things to see, and at night time we felt completely safe to wander around at 3am. There seems to be a high presence of security guards dotted around.Coming back late at night or in the day time was simple and cheap by using taxi, the hotel shuttle bus to Hankow Rd, or ferries to North Point or Central. For those of you staying up late with jet lag, there is a good selection of tv channels in the room to keep you busy. And you can order snacks through the night,One morning we had the breakfast buffet in the room, it was tasty and a wide selection, although I would not have paid that amount to eat it each morning, as it wouldn't be worth it.it would be extremley hard to find fault with the hotel or it's staff.Hope everyone else has a magical and trouble free stay like I did ^^

<Author>S3CR3T3X3C
<Content>Great hotel, will stay again The Harbour plaza is a godsend in expensive Hong Kong: a great hotel with fine, clean, modern rooms with well above average service. My family and I stayed here recently and I am absolutely sure we'll be back. What we liked: - great quiet location right on the harbor - overall price was great for what we got - close to star ferry - very clean, modern and efficient - nice people, good service and very helpful staff - very close via taxi to Tsimshatsui / Mongkok What we did not like so much: - nickle and diming on fees/charges --every thing is an extra fee (we could not get breakfast included or airport pickup or laundry or internet...). These costs balloon quickly which is, I am sure, what they were intending :-(- large business convention type crowds -- we were there when a huge Russian sales group descended on the hotel...- the rooftop pool is a teeny little job which does have great views (actually incredible views...) but is about the size of a child's wading pool in many places I have visited. I would like to add that the Harbour Plaza is a solid 4+ star hotel but if you've stayed at the HKG Grand Hyatt or the Island Shangri La you may be a little disappointed. There is a certain finesse/luxury orientation that is missing. As in any places in Hong Kong, there is a lot of mirror, marble, chrome and shiny glass but perhaps not the overall finish one would expect of a 5 star place in the Orient. That said, this is where we wil stay when we go to HKG again. We liked this place.
