<Author>Niffud
<Content>Believe the reviews Having not been to Hong Kong before and not knowing the lie of the land this was a bit of a stab in the dark, based on reading lots of traveller reviews. I can't remember why I finally plumped for the Harbour Plaza Hong Kong, and when I worked out where the hotel was I was (Hunghom, Kowloon) a little worried, but this was proven to be completely unfounded. We arrived at the hotel early - around 7 am and were therefore able to check in but not able to have our room until midday. We were offered another room, but decided to wait until our pre-booked room was ready (this did of course mean that we had five hours after an eleven hour flight wandering around HK in the same clothes...). Just enough time to visit a tailor and arrange to have a bespoke dress made for the following day.The room, on the eight floor (fortuitous, eh?), did not disappoint. We had a perfect view out over the harbour and it's traffic, and the most vital component in any room, the bed, was just lovely. The pool's as it looks in the pictures, but I have to confess that it was a little too breezy up on the roof when we were there to try it. The fitness suite is also very impressive.The breakfast is good (if a little pricey), but there's lots of choice and you can have as much as you want - although I wouldn't go for the room service option - this was a little sparce.The guys on the door are charming and will help you with most things with that touch of inside knowledge that you need when a stranger in town, and the fact that the hotel practically has its own Star Ferry pier, just tops it all off. There's a shuttle bus that drops off in TST and cabs are cheap so there's no problem with getting around. Do make sure that you've made arrangements for getting back to the airport though since our taxi was a surprising $HK 333.I have not stayed elsewhere in Hong Kong but would not object to having my room overlooking the harbour returned to me as I left it two weeks ago. Twas just what we needed.

<Author>san_diego_travels
<Content>Fabulous Service, Fantastic Hotel We booked our Harbourview room through the Hotel's website after reading the reviews on TripAdvisor. After visiting polluted, hectic Beijing, staying in Hong Kong at the quiet, off-the-beaten path Harbour Plaza was a real treat! The Harbour Plaza has gorgeous views from the moment you enter the hotel. We were cordially greeted by reception, the concierge was always beyond helpful, and the buffet breakfast was varied and delicious (not cheap, but worth it if you're hungry).The view from our room was to die for, and spacious. The bathroom was large with a separate tub and shower. Only minus was the lack of free wireless internet (of course you can pay for access).And the pool is, of course, fantastic! As you will read in almost every review... The hotel is VERY conveniently located to the Star Ferry, which we took to Central, and while that neighborhood is fun, I was so happy to be staying in the more quiet Whampoa district at Harbour Plaza. We had tea at Hong Kong's Peninsula and Mandarin Oriental hotels, and I can tell you that Harbour Plaza easily rivals-- if not exceeds-- both in terms of ambiance and customer service. My friend even got her Chinese visas taken care of by the hotel while we were out sightseeing! Overall, an excellent experience and a GREAT value for the price. I can't wait to visit Hong Kong again and will definitely stay at Harbour Plaza!

<Author>raquelrattle
<Content>More like a 4 star than a 5 star I stayed at this hotel with my mum for 6 nights in May 2007. Overall, we felt the hotel deserved a 4 star rating; we have stayed in plenty of 5 star hotels and this one just didn't stand up to those.Good things about this hotel:1. The hotel is in a decent enough area with plenty of shops and restaurants within walking distance - two supermarkets about 2 mins walk away. 2. There is a star ferry terminal about 2 mins walk away from which you can get ferries to Central and Wan Chai. 3. The courtesy bus runs every 30 mins from about 7am to 11pm and drops you by The Peninsula hotel, but even so, a taxi only costs about 拢2.50!4. The hotel is on the harbourfront and there are only a few hotels in HK that can boast that.5. A roof top swimming pool giving amazing views.6. The hotel is in a quiet location with a proper forecourt so when you step out of the front door you are not straight onto a busy road like you would be if you stayed anywhere in Tsim Sha Tsui or Central.HOWEVER, we had a BIG problem with the lights in our room. The majority of lights are controlled by an electronic touch pad by the bed and our lights kept coming on on their own, in the middle of the night! The first night, we thought maybe we had done it in our sleep or something! However, by the second night, after being woken up SIX times by this, I asked housekeeping to have a look at them - this was about 9.30am. About 9pm that night when we returned to the hotel I phoned housekeeping and asked if someone had looked at the lights. I didn't explain to that particular person what the problem was though, however, he seemed to know the problem very well indeed! Anyway, no-one had looked at the lights and they sent an engineer (please bear in mind that this was 12 horus after my first request). He fiddled with something, said it was fixed and went. Ten minutes later, the lights came on again! The engineer came back and fiddled with something else. Ten minutes later, the lights come on again. By this time, it was 11pm and I had run out of patience. I spoke to the duty manager who arranged for us to change rooms, but because of the late hour, we got very little sleep. Plus the aircon unit was very noisy.I am convinced that the hotel knew about the problem with the lights in that room, but still put us in there. I would love to hear from anyone who had the same problem!The breakfast buffet was average and we chose to stick to a continental breakfast as the sausages looked anaemic and the bacon was full of fat. The waiter topped my cup of tea up with coffee and then gave me a funny look when I asked for a fresh cup with tea in it. Ten minutes later, he did the same thing to my mum's cup of tea!The evening buffet was quite good though and not at all expensive.The hotel host a lot of weddings which was nice to see, however because they use the first floor mezzanine area as the reception area, if you want to go to the lounge bar (on the first floor) you have no choice but to walk through someone's wedding reception!A small word of warning - a lady's handbag was stolen from the cafe bar on the ground floor. She told me that someone distracted her and then someone else took her bag.

<Author>SanFranciscoExplorer
<Content>Harbour Plaza excellent value and oasis We booked the Harbour Plaza after reading solid, positive reviews on Trip Advisor. We are expecting a high standard and were not disappointed by the hotel or the staff.First: after we reserved and paid through Expedia, (which usually results in the worst room in the house, in this case an obstructed, partial view), the staff obligingly changed our room to a full harbour view. Then: when an emergency at home forced us to change our tickets and return a day early, the staff at the business center spent hours making all the arrangements. The women there are the most capable travel coordinators I have ever experienced at a hotel and I've been travelling internationally on business for 30 years!Many reviews talk about the location being out of the way. It's true, that after taking the Star Ferry back late at night, the WanChai docks are closed and you must go to the Kowloon docks then take a cab back to the hotel. This is a 10 minute inconvenience. All other times, the WanChai docks are, literally, a 2 minute walk from the hotel front door - but, around a building's corner so aesthetically out of sight. Cabs are plentiful. The hotel has a free shuttle to Airport Express that runs every 12 minutes. Very convenient for departure.We experienced the hotel's location as an asset. The harbour location is spectacular. There is no traffic noise. We were 2 business women travelling together and we felt absolutely safe and comfortable. I would have felt comfortable staying there alone.The setting of the Harbour Plaza is lovely. I particularly appreciated being in an urban hotel but looking out the window and not seeing building across the street. The overall feeling is that of an oasis. I loved the feeling of openess. The hotel feels like a resort, right in the middle of Hong Kong.The rooftop pool is a pleasure. Don't miss it.We upgraded to the concierge floor and ate breakfast in the club room. It was only OK. Tasty selection but limited variety. The buffet in the gorgeous lobby downstairs, directly on the water, looks delicious, but we never tried it.The room was business-upscale. Very comfortable. Normal and what you would expect from a 5 star in Hong Kong. Unlike the beds throughout most of China which are rock-hard, these beds were blissfully comfortable. Great pillows. Our room had 2 queen-sized beds and a generous, attractive bathroom. Great shower.Uniformly, the staff was attentive, cooperative, eager to be of service, knowledgeable and a pleasure to interact with. If you have tourist hours, don't miss the Hong Kong Museum of History. After 4 hours there, I was hungry for more! A big surprise as I expected to be in-out and on to the next attraction. We also enjoyed the Bird Market. Skip the Temple Street Market which is a junk-pile of cheap, tourist items. The Stanley Street Market isn't much better but the ride to get there is interesting.We found a private guide on the web and found a day with him to be invaluable. Facinating information on history and also present-day life in Hong Kong. I highly recommend a day's walking tour of Central.Another reviewer wrote that the air pollution in Hong Kong is omnipresent. This is true. A plume of bad air from the manufacturing centers in Guangzhou and its industrial corridor washes down across Hong Kong. It's surprising that the air quality there is so poor considering that the city is on the ocean. You can easily read local opinions. The air quality is becoming a serious issue for business recruitment as people with young families don't wish to have their children exposed to this level of pollution. The week before we were there, the head of the HK Philharmonic Orchestra quit because he needed to take his children to a cleaner city.That said, we had a marvelous time in Hong Kong on a business trip with a couple of tourist days added on. The Harbour Plaza was a large part of our positive experience. Highly recommended!  
<Date>May 14, 2007

<Content>Beautiful Hotel - amazing views After much researching, I booked this hotel through whotif.com and felt like I got a great deal. <Author>TravelcatsSF
<Content>Total disapointment Read all the reviews.My family and I stayed at the Harbour Plaza on our way from Tokyo to Bangkok. While we stayed at much nicer hotels in those cities, the cost to stay at the HP was much more. We reserved a Harbor View room. Upon arriving at the HP, we were given a key to our room. Nobody showed us the way. When the door to the elevator opened on our designated floor, we were overwhelmed by the smell of new paint or solvent. Our room, while clean, had what they call in the real estate business, a peek-a-boo view of the harbor. We were set back from the water by several hundred feet and had to look between two buildings to see Hong Kong. The Bell Boy arrived after 45 minutes with our bags and commanded my 9 year old daughter to get out of the way as he dropped the bags.I asked if there was a better room, and was told that the hotel was fully booked. Highly doubtful.Basically, there was NO service at all. Like staying at the Holiday in at the airport.One night, after trekking through the city all day, we decided we should have dinner at the hotel. They offer a buffet in the lobby. The cost is $45 dollars [US] per person. I think they said my daughter would be $35. Maybe I'm not a big spender, but $125 bucks for a buffet in the middle of the week is pretty high. The hotel is situated right on the water, and has nice views of Hong Kong. While the buffet area seats well over 100 people, there were less that 15 people seated. We were rushed to our seats located six rows in from the windows. I said to the host that we would like to sit at one of the 20 tables which sat empty at the windows. With a swift wave of his arm, he said NO! I asked again politely, why we couldn't move to the window, and again, he waved his hand across his body with a stern NO!Well. Enough for us. We left.After several days at the HP, we flew to Bangkok to stay at the Peninsula. It's like eating one day at Pizza Hut Express and the next at a Michelin Three Star restaurant!Would NOT recommend the Harbour Plaza!

<Author>MisterThirty
<Content>Fantastic!!!! This is a superb hotel! I booked this hotel a few months ago to celebrate my 30th birthday in Hong Kong and I was not disappointed. Hung Hom is a little out of the way from the main thoroughfares but do not let this deter you. Once you have got the airport shuttle to Kowloon, there is a signposted bus that swiftly takes you from Kowloon to your hotel. This is efficiency that you quickly get used to in Hong Kong. In terms of transport to other parts of the city there is naturally the ferry opposite to Wan Chai and Central (until 7pm) on HK Island as well as a shuttle bus that drops you off in Kowloon (until 11pm) plus lots of cheap taxis (think 拢6 max late at night to get back from Central). The room was very comfortable and tasteful with nice soft beds. The room we booked had a harbour view on the 8th floor (good for Chinese luck) so it was great for jet lagged mornings looking out in bed at the boats passing by! I was wide-awake some mornings at 5am so went out of the hotel and saw a few locals doing their Tai Chi. Great atmosphere! In terms of room service, there always seemed to be someone on hand to sort out our beds after a jetlag nap beyond 8pm. I also got a nice cake for my birthday from the hotel.The pool was excellent with lovely views and was well heated. I went swimming a couple of times there. The gym facilities were also very good as well with helpful staff and with great treadmills. I did not eat much in the hotel but the Waterfront Grill cooked me probably the best steak sandwich in my life. It was totally delicious. In terms of other useful things to know: The reception can organise coach tours of various places in Hong Kong. I did an afternoon trip to Lantau Island which cost about 拢28. It was excellent and for somebody new to Hong Kong I would recommend taking a tour. Also there is a Pacific Coffee Company Store (like Costa Coffee) half a block away serving pastries, coffees, sandwiches and salads. This was very useful for getting a quick Westernised snack and cheaper than room service.The only problem with this hotel is that you might not want to leave it! Hong Kong is one of the World's great cities so you just need to make sure you head out and enjoy it.

<Author>Robwash
<Content>What's the catch Stayed 2 nights on the way to other parts of S.E. Asia. My wife and I wanted to get over the jet lag after a very long flight. The hotel, I thought, was almost too good to be true given the glowing reports on Trip Advisor and the great looking pictures provide by the hotel. In short, all the positive comments are true, and the hotel really does look as good as the pictures. If this hotel were located near Nathan Road with the same waterfront location, rooms would easily cost twice as much (or more). This is the only real issue with the hotel.....its distance from the heart of Kowloon. As previously noted, there is a shuttle bus running every half hour that takes about 10 minutes and drops you off at the Peninsula (you easily pick up the shuttle in the same spot). The shuttles run like clockwork and are very reliable. There is also a shuttle running 4 times and hour to Kowloon station where you get the train to the airport. The only other issue I can think of is the harbour view from the rooms. Our view was very good, but given the hotel's location it isn't the picture-postcard view of Hong Kong island you see in postcards. But it is a view that's worth paying for.So for those who want a quintessential Hong Kong Harbor view from their room, or for those who want to be more within walking distance of the Star Ferry and the major shopping venues (and not rely on a shuttle), this may not be for you. Otherwise, this is a great and friendly hotel and a truely fantastic value.

<Author>stayklassy
<Content>Lovely hotel, wonderful location This is a large, modern hotel on the harbour in Kowloon. It's in Hung Hom, which is away from the bright lights and busy atmosphere of the hotels of Tsim Tsa Sui and Nathan Rd. but it's a lovely oasis in a busy, hectic city. The hotel runs a shuttle every 30 minutes that will take you into TST (where you can catch a subway or go shopping or explore on foot). It's a very well-run, clean property with elegant spacious rooms. We booked it as a package with Cathay Pacific, and got a big room with a queen bed, a sofa, table and desk area. The views of the harbour are beautiful, as the hotel is perched right over the waterfront. The neighbourhood (Whampoa) is still full of amenities - lots of very good shops and restaurants including a Pacific Coffee shop up the street, and an amazing supermarket/dept. store, Jusco, where you can buy everything from a delicious take-out meal (for a criminially low price) to household items, clothing, souvenirs, you name it. The Hung Hom ferry terminal is about a 3 minute walk from the hotel, and the Star Ferry takes you over to Central from there. There's also a big bus zone where you can catch buses around the city close by. Would definitely stay here again, and would choose it over most hotels in the city, including the famed Peninsula (the Harbour Plaza's lobby felt way more elegant than the Penninsula's, which was crowded and loud.)  
<Date>Jan 28, 2007

<Author>chalkntalk
<Content>We didn't want to leave! What a place for a stopover! I was travelling to Sydney with my husband and two children, aged 12 and 13, and chose the Harbour plaza because of Trip Advisor reviews. They are not wrong. After a long flight it is fantastic to have such luxury. It is also in a fantastic location - with shops and lots of restaurants. Do not be put off eating at the restaurants just because they have no English outside. Inside most seem to have English translations, or at least one person who can help out. We particularly liked the Moon Chiu (spelling?) on the corner very close to the hotel. We were treated like royalty and the food was very good - and exceptionally good value. The food court offers lots of choice, though we found it better to eat there at lunch time as in the evening it was packed! Our last afternoon/evening was amazing. We went up to the Peak visited Madam Tussaud's - very different to London's. There are lots of models to interest westerners and you can actually get up close and have your picture taken with them. It was very interactive and not too busy. Kids loved it. We then did a lovely short walk around the Peak and went for an evening meal. We booked Cafe Deco restaurant before we left England. It was fab. We had a table inside overlooking the Harbour (see Frommer's website for advice on booking).We all adored Hong Kong and hope to go back again.  
<Date>Jan 17, 2007

<Author>UKPenpusher
<Content>Wonderful place to stay - no exceptions!! I booked this hotel through a travel agent, after arranging my own itinerary that took in Singapore, muliple centres in Australia and finally, Hong Kong. As we were travelling in low season, we got an automatic upgrade as part of the package. I had read some great reviews, and they actually didn't do the hotel justice, it was a dream stay.I stayed with my six year old son, who took full advantage of room service and the roof-top swimming pools (one is specifically for children). The hotel is beautifully positioned, on the waterfront (perfect for muggy days), and the sight through the full length glass windows of the harbour when you first enter the hotel takes your breath away. The staff were fantastic, incredibly helpful, and the free shuttle bus to various locations around Hong Kong made getting around easy. The hotel is also close to a Star Ferry terminal, ideal for crossing over to Hong Kong island.I didn't choose to use the hotel's many restaurants (six year olds can be a bit too unpredictable!!), however, we used room service on several occasions, and this worked out beautifully. Alternatively, Whampoa Gardens shopping mall is close by, and there are many restaurants and food outlets there of all nationalities, so you're bound to find something you like. The hotel is very smart, and is used both by business people and tourists, and so there is always a mix of people in different attire in the lobby. There is also a coffee shop in the lobby (this is a good-sized hotel), and the hotel has it's own patisserie. These cakes and the sandwiches made to order were also of the highest quality.All in all, this hotel is very luxurious. The staff are helpful, courteous and the food good. Location was perfect for me, in that it is a short (free) shuttle bus ride to the major Kowloon shopping areas of Tsim Shat Sui, airport (extra cost), and the nearest MTR (tube)  KTR (train) stations. It is easy to get around, access to central areas is easy, yet the hotel is positioned in a quiet area, one I appreciated even more when I was actually there. The view from our harbour view room was fascinating - the waterway is very busy, with junks, tourist boats, ferries and container ships all passing our windows.Facilites provided were good - gym, swimming pool etc, and the view from the rooftop infinity pool over Hong Kong Island is one I shall never forget.. I long to return.

<Author>dantatjai
<Content>Excellent Hotel The rooms are clean and quite roomy. I was worried that the rooms were going to be small since I only booked regular rooms, but it turned out to be pretty good. It can be tight if you have 4 ppl in one room. We had only two and it was totally fine. The service was pretty good at the front desk, they were pretty helpful and nice. You can take it to Central, WanChai and NorthPoint. It's faster than mtr. The area has lots of shopping and good restaurants. There's also a delicious bakery down the block where i get breakfast almost every morning. THere's also a famous dessert place around the area too. In terms of location, the only bad thing is that it's not close to one. It's about 5 mins cab or bus ride away. But this is the place to be if you want to be away from the crowd in the morning. The hotel area is very residential so it's not packed when you walk downstairs. If you walk further out (1-2 blocks), you get all the stores you need like shopping, restaurants, 7-11, pharmacy, etc. Excellent stay and I will definitely go back again!

<Author>Softspikes
<Content>Harbour is a bit of heaven I selected the Harbour Plaza based on reviews found here on Tripadvisor.com, and they couldn't have been more accurate. What a lovely, tranquil, well appointed place this is with an abiding staff. Being away from the TST is a plus for me, though the hotel shuttle can get you there in 15 minutes with its every half-hour service. Ferry terminal is a short walk away, and so is the Whampoa shopping district which has lovely restaurants and stores.  My room, a harbor view on the 18th floor, was gorgeous. I never heard a single sound on my floor, but when I left at 7 in the morning for a ferry ride, nearly every door had a newspaper hanging from it, indicating the place was pretty well sold out.I suspect the Harbour Plaza restaurants are fine, but I prefer to eat outside of a hotel and the Whampoa Gourmet Market has a lovely Chinese restaurant with very good dim sum at a very reasonable price. The area has a long waterfront walk and several greenspaces and couldn't be more abiding. This was my first visit to Hong Kong and I will definitely return. The Harbour Plaza will always be my hotel.Jeff Williams, New York

<Author>Geebee2
<Content>Wow, 10 out of 10 We chose the Harbour Plaza Hong Kong for our holiday in October primarily because of the great write-ups it has received on this site, and, wow, am I glad I discovered TripAdvisor. This hotel is just beautiful and certainly deserves all the accolades which have been laid upon it here.I had been intending to write something about our stay but somehow the days drifted past since our return and I guess I felt it was simply too late to comment. However, when I read the rather negative comments by Sspade I just had to get the fingers hitting the keyboard. I can't believe he thought the hotel more tourist orientated than business. While we were there the hotel was full, and, sure the guests seemed to arrive by the busload, but that was because so many of them were delegates of conferences and trade fairs which were happening at the time. This is definitely not a touristy hotel, witnessed by the fact that it pops up in very few travel brochures or even on the tourist maps of Hong Kong. In all of our 12 night stay I think we only saw two families there with children, and most of the guests we spoke to - or overheard - were there on business. Sspade's comments about the smells and noise in the foyer area leave me a tad mystified also.Anyway, back to the hotel. Check-in was absolutely seamless, and - wonderfully - our suitcases were delivered to our room within about 5 minutes. Our room was large and, with an upgrade to a harbour view, had spectacular views over the harbour to the island - gorgeous at night. The room was made up at least twice a day, with the staff ensuring that we had plenty of tea and coffee making provisions - often overlooked - and supplying plenty of free bottled water. The meals we ate at the hotel were fantastic, and the dinner we enjoyed on one particular evening at the Waterfront Bar  Grill next door (part of the hotel's facilities) was absolutely memorable.One of the great things about this hotel is its location - away from the bustle of Nathan Road. The hotel is in a very nice area of Kowloon which boasts some fantastic shopping centres. Ladies, the boutiques here are just wonderful with none of the junky stuff found at Mongkok. Another great feature is the close proximity of an excellent supermarket where we were even able to buy fresh milk daily - all the way from Australia - plus things like bandaids, munchies to go with our drinks, headache pills etc.We certainly wouldn't contemplate staying anywhere else in Hong Kong after this visit, so thanks to all the members here whose comments drew us to this property.

<Author>Sangha
<Content>Excellent Hotel My husband and I recently stayed at the Harbour Plaza Hong Kong. Couldnt do enough for us This hotel is situated v close to the star ferry,there is a free shuttle bus down town (10 mins) and taxis are V V cheap. But the bonus is that it is away from the HKG maelstrom and quiet. Tip go there!!

<Author>Madrava
<Content>Beautiful Hotel, lovely location We stayed at the Harbour Plaza as part of UK company Travelmood's 'Hot Deal' package - three nights 拢214 per person including bus transfers and full day trip to Macau. Incredible deal. Unfortunately due to a typhoon we only managed two nights and they were wonderful. The hotel is grand but comfortable and was hosting a couple of weddings so it was lovely to see the magnificent marble staircase bedecked with organza and roses. We ordered a big breakfast in our room costing about 220 HK each and it came delivered on table with white napery and silver service. Delicious.The bed was one of the most comfortable we have ever slept in and as we had asked for a harbour view it was wonderful to sit and watch the dawn rising and the coming to life of the harbour as the cruise boats and ferries and junks sailed past. There is a lovely walkway surrounding the hotel and we watched the locals doing Tai Chi in the morning. Next door at the Waterfront bar we enjoyed cocktails as it was Happy Hour (two drinks for one from 6 until 7.30) Harbour Plaza is a peaceful place and the star ferry is right on the doorstep although two crossings are necessary to get to Harbour City mall. Since we love the ferry so much we did not bother with the hotel shuttle service.

After a few telephone calls later, they telephoned the hotel again and said they were very concerned and would have to telephone the police. The hotel then discovered that I had booked but cancelled my booking the day before. When I heard all the commotion on my answerphone on my return, I asked the hotel myself whether I had booked in, giving my name. They repeated that I had cancelled my booking and never checked in. When I revealed my true identity, all they could do was look sheepish. I am just glad there was not an emergency at home and my mobile telephone was not in fact lost.2 The breakfast was included in the price. However, we were not told that it had to be taken in a certain part of the hotel, otherwise you wer charged. Nor were we told at what time breakfast was served until. They telephoned the airline as we stood there waiting. When the number was engaged, they gave up and handed us back the flight details. For a comparison of this service in another HK hotel, see my review of the Langham Hotel.5 Generally, this hotel is out of the way but doesn't go out of its way to help. Perhaps we were just unlucky. For over 拢100 a night, we didn't think it was worth it and on our return went to stay at the Langham Hotel - also reviewed on this website.

<Author>Bazza61
<Content>Only hotel in HK to stay at! For those Aussies reading this, I booked through Harvey World Travel - got 5 nights for the cost of 4 , plus upgrade to Harbour View room and buffet breakfast. Cost me $200 AUD per night - good deal IMO. The hotel is 41/2 star, very clean, excellent attentiveness from all the staff and exceptionally well located (for me). Hong Kong was VERY hot and it is a really busy, noisy, hectic city-so the location of this hotel right on the waterfront (there are a few others but much more expensive) and some distance out of the mayhem of the more popular? areas of both Kowloon and Hong Kong Island make this for me the only hotel to stay at in HK ( for that price). The regular bus hotel bus shuttle every 30 minutes to downtown Kowloon (drops off next to YMCA) works well - and there is a Star Ferry terminal for rides to HK Island only a couple of minutes walk away from the front door. The Airport Express train from the airport works well - get off at Kowloon Station and get the K1 free bus from there to the hotel. All in all, I cannot recommend this hotel highly enough - great value for money.

<Author>adejejon
<Content>Good value for money Wife and I stayed May 27 to Jun 02 in Club room with fantastic views overlooking Harbour(18th Floor). Room adequate size, with sofa and work desk. Maid service good. Club lounge small but adequate. Mislead by description in hotel guide of all-day refreshments. In fact, complimentary refreshments only available at breakfast(7-10), afternoon tea(3-6) and early evening(6-8).Only tried Whampoa Lounge and Waterfront Restaurant. Don't miss latter, since it is outside the hotel on the way towards ferry terminal, but provides reasonably priced food and drinks. Happy hour early evening.Regular free coach shuttle to Kowloon shopping area, behind Peninsula Hotel. We also made much use of ferry service to Hong Kong Island(Central), but beware last ferry returns at about 7pm. Many high-class(and expensive) malls on Hong Kong Island. Cheaper(much!) street markets in Kowloon. You should be able to bargain at least 50% off initial price on fake bags etc. For clothing try G2000, Crocodile and Giordano shops, shirts from 5GBP. Do try trip to Stanley Market for souvenirs.Take airport express rail service, as preference to road travel, savings can be made by booking in advance.Sadly, it rained every day, and roof-top pool mostly closed due threat of lightning!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great position fabulous facilities I stayed at this hotel on two seperate occasions as I used this as my stopover hotel en route to and from Australia. The hotel is really impressive with fabulous public areas and was clearly popular as a wedding venue. The hotel rooms were spacious with good sized bathrooms. <Author>jj-the-jetsetter
<Content>Great position if you have a harbour view room We stayed here after a 14 day tour of China, and were on a package, so don't know what the costs were. Having read reviews before we went, we were pleased to have a harbour view room, which was very spacious with bath and shower and all the usual extras. Drinks from the mini-bar were expensive but there is a 7-11 just up the street opposite, also a good laundry as the hotel laundry prices were astronomical.There are also a good variety of restaurants locally(including an excellent Australian steak bar - the Outback - just the thing after 14 days eating nothing but Chinese food on our tour!), so we didn't eat in, and therefore can't comment. Superb friendly, helpful staff, spotless, well-designed and spacious public rooms and bedroom, super pool on top - worth a visit just for the view. The aircon is VERY fierce.Hung Hom is less touristy, and as others have stated, but the (lesser) ferry terminal is next door. If you are there are on Sunday and don't mind American Evangelical Christianity, you will have an excellent welcome at the Church opposite in the school complex, and an interesting service. The shuttle bus worked perfectly.

<Author>Lemniot
<Content>Great cakes! Difficult one this!Unlike the previous reviewers who mostly seem to love this hotel, I have mixed feelings. Nothing I can really put my finger on. I have to rate it highly, because it is such an attractive, well run operation but I did not massively enjoy my stay. Maybe it was just too big for me? Maybe because we could have had a slightly better room for the money?It is a little out of the way in a very quiet but pretty harbourside spot with an attractive walkway/promenade in front. The views are sensational but then all the views in Hong Kong are! We liked the position (on balance) because of the peace and quiet and because it was close to the other Star Ferry, the one that takes three times as long to get across to HK Island. The free shuttle was a boon and we used it most days.It is certainly not a cheap hotel but then the service is exemplary, the rooms are very smart and clean and it is worth splashing out on a harbour view but avoid our room 637 or any other -37, where the view - though still amazing - was slightly restricted. The gym was brilliant with every sort of facility and the rooftop pool was pretty sensational and we had great pleasure using it. I found the Business Centre very helpful and not expensive to use, though I suspect it helps that I am not one of those heavy businessmen types that demand a lot and are very curt to the staff. Best of all - the lovely cakes and pastries in the small bakery/cafe downstairs. Well had to have a reason to go to the gym!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Out of the way but nice views I had a decent stay recently at the Harbour Plaza Hong Kong. I knew the hotel was in Kowloon, but I was surprised when the airport shuttle dropped me off. This hotel is not in the tourist area of Tsim Sha Tsui, but east of there in Hung Hom. Luckily, the hotel has efficient shuttle bus service to the center, or better yet, there is a star ferry terminal at Hung Hom nearby (if you are going to Central HK). In the end, I liked staying away from the hords of tourist and commuting in with the locals, but be aware of this, if like me, you are thinking this hotel in in a central location. I had several problems at check in, I requested non-smoking and got smoking, I booked a harbour view and got a courtyard view, I was suppose to get breakfast and they said no. It got worked out more or less, but I still got a smoking room and on the first floor for guests. The room was just OK, a little musty and old in spots. But even on the lower floor, the harbour view was fantastic! This place is all about the view, there is just no reason to book a courtyard view here. Spend the extra dollars. Breakfast was quite good with alot of variety. There are nice areas to walk along the harbour, and the shopping area of Whampoa Gardens has everything you'll need for food and snacks.

<Author>KCKansasCity
<Content>Fair! My husband two teenagers and I stayed at the Harbour Plaza recently and left after one night. We booked connecting harbour view rooms for our stay and only one was ready when we checked in at 6pm. We were told that the other had plumbing problems, but we were able to get into both rooms at 7pm that evening. While we were waiting for our room we had dinner in the main restaurant on the lobby level. We were the only ones in the restaurant and the service was terribly slow. There were cigarette ashes on the place mats, and the food was fair at best. Our rooms seemed fine, and had a nice view of the harbour. My husband tried to hook up his laptop computer but there was nothing to plug it into. He called the business center (the phone rang over 20 times), and they sent up a cable which had to be stretched across the room. All seemed to be well until he tried to send email messages. The computer connection cut out and he lost 50 percent of the work that he had been doing. This happened repeatedly. The rooms and linens smelled of smoke and a flowery air freshener that was used to mask it. It didn;t work. The duvet on the king bed did not cover the width of the bed, and the bedspread on top of it was smelly and pilled. After finally falling asleep housekeeping barged into our room (without knocking or announcing themselves) for turn down service. This hotel would be fine for those who are strictly tourists and on a limited budget, however as my husband found out the hard way the conditions are very primitive for those trying to conduct business from their room. The staff was okay, but didn't make any unnecessary effort (i.e. the doorman was busy talking with his co-workers most of the time). Overall it was not a horrible experience, but everything about the Harbour Plaza seemed just FAIR.

<Author>bshort4
<Content>Could not ask for better.... Spent three nights in this hotel from March 7th to 10th and was most impressed. From the greeting at the front door to the speedy check-in service and the lovely room I could not have asked for more. I booked a harbour view room that had a huge window facing the harbour which is right next to the hotel. The room is of good size with a lovely bathroom and the beds were very soft for Hong Kong. Room included a pot to boil water for either tea or coffee which were complimentry in the room. The bathrooms include everything you need in case you forgot something---from combs to razors to toothbrushs and robes and slippers. All the hotel personnel speak perfect English and are eager to assist you with any problem or request you might have. The rooftop pool is great even though we didn't have a chance to use it because the weather was a bit chilly but the views from there were outstanding. The hotel is alittle off the beaten path in a quiet neighborhood which was nice. We found a lovely coffee shop a block from the hotel with great coffee and pastries and free computers to use if you bought something to drink. The hotel runs a free shuttle every half hour to downtown Kowloon for shopping or for getting on the subway system. A ferry pier is a three minute walk from the hotel to catch the ferry across the harbour to Hong kong for about .40 cents USA. They also have shuttle busses that stop there and take you to the Airport Express train for free. We paid about $130 American per night for the harbour view room through Asia Rooms, non harbour view rooms would be less expensive. If you want a great hotel to stay in that you will not be disappointed in you can't go wrong with the Harbour Plaza Hong Kong. Please do not confuse it with the other Harbour View hotels like the Metropolis (sp) which are not as nice.

<Author>iGuy
<Content>Great Place to Relax  The tail end of a 2 month trip throughout SE Asia found us with 4 nights in HK so as frequent Tripadvisor users we factored in the previous reviews and chose the Harbour Plaza. We booked using an online site and got a great rate for HK!We were somewhat trepidatious of the locale but the moment we pulled up the entrance driveway, were greeted by the Indian Doorman and witnessed the incredible harbour view through the wall of glass we knew we were in the right place. Our check in was smooth (thanks Queenie!) and our side harbourview room was just what we needed.Our standard room was very large(especially by HK standards)and in perfect condition. The king bed was so comfortable that we routinely slept in quite late. The rooftop pool and fitness center are first rate(what a view!)and the twice an hour free shuttle got us right downtown onto Nathan road in just a few minutes.Unfortunately the restaurants, minibar and business center are very pricey. A USD$5 can of coke or USD$10 bottle of water is simply unreasonable as is the Internet access at USD$6 for 15 mins. Luckily you just have to step outside into the Whampoa Gardens neighborhood where you can eat drink and surf quite affordably.Great housekeeping, incredible staff and fabulous service make this a wonderful hotel and we will undoubtedly consider it again on our next trip to Hong Kong.

<Content>Good Overall Experience We spent 5 nights at the end of January with a harbor view room.Upon checkin the hotel wanted a cash deposit (we try to not use credit cards) and was willing to accept a smaller than normal USD deposit until we could get HKD the next day. <Author>fifibell
<Content>Great quality at decent prices The Harbour Plaza is a very good hotel at a more reasonable price, presumably due to being slightly further out than other hotels of a similar standard. There is nothing particularly unique about this hotel but it is suitably grand with a stunning sweeping staircase and the obligatory fountains and columns. The room (a large harbour view double) was extremely spacious and smartly furnished. The only slight disappointment was the harbour view from our room which was not quite the harbour view of hong kong island as we had a corner room looking away from the main harbour area.All in all, a good find if you want to stay in a top end hotel and don't mind the minor inconvenience of taking the shuttle bus to and from the centre. Taxis are also very cheap so it is not a problem even once the shuttle has stopped at 11.30 pm.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Loved the Harbour Plaza HK - Very Romantic Hotel My husband and I stayed at this beautiful hotel just this past month, for 6 days. Would definitely return. Although the hotel had all the standard modern amenities (for business travellers) the harbourside location, traditional style furnishings and excellent service lent the place a more old world, elegant, feel. Lobby was absolutely stunning. Floor to ceiling glass window (at least 2 stories high)with an unobstructed harbour view. Staff was knowledgeable, efficient, courteous and spoke amazing English. Rooms are very big by HK standards - bathroom even has a stereo system connected to the TV. Had a glass of wine on the patio our first night - very romantic setting. We found the location to be a plus rather than a drawback - after a very hectic day it was so relaxing to retreat to somewhere quiet. The Whampoa district is also a better opportunity to get a better feel for local life if you walk around the neighbourhood - much preferable to touristy TST or Central. We felt we were living among the locals and could actually observe people going to school nearby or getting their groceries..etc. - these experiences added a more intimate and enriching feel to our stay in HK. In addition the air quality at the hotel location was noticeably better than in either TST or Central.The one drawback we found was that the hotel buffet breakfast was a bit expensive for not a great variety of items to select from although what we did get was a top quality mix of Western and Chinese standard breakfast items. It was also amazing experience to have your coffee and croissant accompanied by an unobstructed view of HK harbour as the city was just waking up. A somewhat zen experience - the buffet area itself (the PROMENADE) was very spacious, located just off the lobby and occupying much of it, and a GREAT place to people watch. A number of Chinese and English daily papers were provided (complementary). No casual Western eateries nearby to grab a more reasonably priced quick breakfast however, I didn't mind since I, being Chinese, just frequented the many Chinese noodle shops in the neighbourhood. (There is also a Maxim's nearby which offers very reasonable Chinese food in a Western environment.)Very efficient, punctual and clean shuttle buses Very courteous shuttle drivers. One of the drivers had a penchant for Air Supply songs, which we found very endearing. Drawback - last shuttle of the day from TST to the hotel is 11:30 pm. Definitely deserves a return stay. Particularly suitable for a romantic getaway.

<Content>An Oasis In A City We stayed for 6 days at Habour Plaza, in kowloon. The Hotel is very elegant and locates right on the water front with magnificient view of the Victoria Habour. The atmosphere is definately upscale. What we like: It provides a great view of HK city-scape at night. Make sure you request a Habour View Room. You will not regret it. It is close by Wompoa District which has many shops and restaurants. It is a quite oasis in a hustle city. The Waichai Ferry is a five minutes walk to catch a ferry over to HK. An evening walk on the water front is a plus. What we did not like: lack of quick cafe style venue to allow for you to catch a quite bite before heading out. The staff could be friendlier. Watch out for your hotel bill--I was charged for a fax service that i did not request (small amount). The interior of the room could be cleaner and need some updating. We will definately return to this hotel in the future.P.S.-make sure you tell taxi driver that this is the Habour Plaza and not the Habour Metropolis (same owner but this one is actually in the business district of Kowloon).

<Author>tearose
<Content>One of the Very Best Hotels in Hong Kong! Just returned from a 24-day trip to Southeast Asia that included stays in five 5-star hotels. All were excellent, but this is the one whose memory keeps coming to mind. (Read the titles of the preceding 10 reviews; all are accurate!)  This is a hotel with a breathtakingly beautiful lobby and location right on the Hong Kong harbor. I never seemed to tire of standing at my wall-to-wall window on the 17th floor and watching all the shipping activity, and the lights across the water on Victoria Island.  It's no wonder that Premier Hu of China has stayed at the Harbour Plaza three times in recent years, including during the British turnover of the territory to China on July 1, 1997. If I were him, I would too. The hotel is heavily favored by wealthy local Hong Kong citizens as well as international travelers. In our brief three-day visit, we observed a number of beautiful Chinese wedding parties, complete with decorated Bentleys, Rolls Royces, etc.  The staff we interacted with were as friendly and efficient as one would hope for in a 5-star establishment. A Mercedes limo transfer to the airport was reasonable by American standards: $64.50 for the 15-mile or so trip.  More than half the rooms at the Harbour Plaza have unimpeded views of the harbor; if you stay here, be sure to get one, unless you don't like spectacular views. The sweeping marble staircase in the lobby is unforgettable; so is the infinity pool on the hotel roof, although the water temperature in late November was just tolerable. The hotel is in a very good area. Immediately adjacent, and matching the hotel's architecture, is a brand new 70-story condominium tower with what are reputed to be the highest prices per square foot in Hong Kong (well, that's what the taxi driver told us). The area (Hung Hom) has a beautiful promenade along the waterfront that is a bit over a mile long. While many other hotels in Hong Kong have harbor views, only the Intercontinental comes to mind as having a similar promenade.  While Hung Hom seems a bit distant from the crowds on Nathan Road and at Ocean Centre, the hotel's free shuttle leaves exactly on the hour and half-hour for the 10-minute trip, with stops at the Shangri-La Kowloon and the Peninsula. The Star Ferry pier to Victoria is a 3-minute walk along the promenade. Hong Kong has many good hotels, each with strong points. However, in addition to its waterfront location, beautiful architecture, and 5-star service, the Harbour Plaza rates extremely well on a price-value ratio. It's really fun to see a place that succeeds so well.  
<Date>Nov 30, 2005
